     <h1 class="toc-ignore">Tumult Hype Documentation</h1> 
     <p>If you’re unfamiliar with Tumult Hype, our documentation is the best way to learn about all of Hype’s amazing features. Get up to speed by reading the other documentation chapters linked on the left side.</p> 
     <h3 id="learn-your-way">Learn your way</h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com">Join our Forums!</a> Over 21 thousand searchable posts on nearly every aspect of <span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span>. </li> 
      <li><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/tutorials/">Watch a few tutorial videos, and explore other learning resources.</a></li> 
      <li>Visit our <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/TumultHype">YouTube Channel</a> to watch all our videos.</li> 
      <li>View the <a href="http://tumult.com/hype/gallery/">Gallery</a> for downloadable examples</li> 
      <li>Download this documentation <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/Tumult%20Hype%20Documentation-3_0.zip">with example documents (39MB)</a>, <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/Tumult%20Hype%20Documentation-3_0_noDocs.zip">without example documents (18MB)</a> or <a target="_blank" href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/Tumult%20Hype%20Documentation.pdf">as a PDF (14MB)</a>. </li> 
     </ul>

        <div class="category"> 
         <div class="icon1"></div> 
         <div class="name">
           Overview 
         </div> 
         <div class="description">
           Tumult Hype 3 is the HTML5 creation app for OS X. Interactive content and animations made with Hype work on desktops, smartphones, and iPads. 
         </div> 
         <div class="links"> 
          <ul> 
           <li> <a href="#overview">User Interface</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#key-terms">Key Terms</a> </li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="category"> 
         <div class="icon2"></div> 
         <div class="name">
           Scenes 
         </div> 
         <div class="description">
           Scenes are a useful way to separate and organize content. They are similar to slides in a Keynote or PowerPoint presentation. 
         </div> 
         <div class="links"> 
          <ul> 
           <li> <a href="#managing-scenes">Managing Scenes</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#changing-scenes">Changing Scenes</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#rulers">Rulers</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#guides">Guides</a> </li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="category"> 
         <div class="icon3"></div> 
         <div class="name">
           Elements 
         </div> 
         <div class="description">
           Elements are the objects in a scene. They can be shapes, text, buttons, textured buttons, images, videos or HTML widgets. 
         </div> 
         <div class="links"> 
          <ul> 
           <li> <a href="#elements">Types of Elements</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#manipulating-elements">Manipulating Elements</a> </li> 
           <li> <a href="#managing-elements">Managing Elements</a> </li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="line-2"> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon6"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Animations 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">
            Tumult Hype uses a powerful keyframe-based animation system to give elements motion and transitions. Its recording functionality makes building animations a snap. 
          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#animation-user-interface">Animation User Interface</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#keyframes">Keyframes</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#recording">Recording</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#manually-editing-keyframes">Manually Editing Keyframes</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#motion-paths">Motion Paths</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#easing-amp-animation-timing-functions">Easing &amp; Animation Timing Functions</a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon7"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Timelines 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">
            Timelines contain animations. Each scene has at least one timeline, scenes can also have many timelines. Using actions to start, pause, or continue timelines creates rich and complex documents. 
          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#managing-timelines">Managing Timelines</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#controlling-timeline-playback">Controlling Timeline Playback</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#absolute-and-relative-keyframes">Absolute and Relative Keyframes</a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon8"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Actions 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">
            Scenes, timelines, and animations are the foundation of all Tumult Hype documents. Actions link together this foundation and make documents interactive. 
          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#mouse-and-touch-actions">Mouse and Touch Actions</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#scene-actions">Scene Actions</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#timeline-actions">Timeline Actions</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#types-of-actions">Type of Actions</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#chaining-actions">Chaining</a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="line-2"> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon16"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Responsive Layout 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">
            Responsive Layouts allows you to create multiple layouts for a single scene which are shown at specific breakpoints. 
          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#creating-new-layouts">Creating New Layouts</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#adjusting-layouts">Adjusting Layouts</a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon9"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Flexible Layout 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">
            A powerful layout system for resizing and scaling documents and elements, Flexible Layouts allows Hype animations to respond as the browser’s window or device’s viewport changes size. 
          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#document-scaling">Document Scaling</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#element-pinning-and-sizing">Element Pinning and Sizing</a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="category"> 
          <div class="icon17"></div> 
          <div class="name">
            Physics 
          </div> 
          <div class="description">

          </div> 
          <div class="links"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#scene-physics-gravity">Scene Physics Gravity</a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#element-physics">Element Physics</a> </li>

     <h1 id="overview">Overview</h1> 
     <p>Tumult Hype is the HTML5 creation app for OS X. Interactive content and animations made with Tumult Hype work on desktops, smartphones, and iPads.</p> 
     <p>Wow your web visitors by making beautiful animated content with Tumult Hype!</p> 
     <p>Tumult Hype is an HTML5 authoring tool. What is commonly referred to as “HTML5” is really a platform of technologies including the latest HTML tags, CSS styles, and improved JavaScript performance. HTML5’s capabilities allow for stunning visual effects and smooth animations, but previously required difficult hand-coding. There were no designer-friendly tools for building animated HTML5 content… until Tumult Hype.</p> 
     <p>Tumult Hype’s powerful keyframe-based animations bring your content to life and outputs state-of-the-art HTML5 that works on all modern browsers and mobile devices like iPhones and iPads. No coding required.</p> 
     <h3 id="tumult-hype-professional">Tumult Hype Professional</h3> 
     <p>Tumult Hype Professional is available as an in-app purchase and adds many powerful features to Hype 3.5:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Waypoint actions for on Viewport Enter/Exit</li> 
      <li>Hype Reflect 2.0 gains responsive preview and dark theme</li> 
      <li>Advanced Export for choosing slices to export specific scenes/layouts/resources</li> 
      <li>Responsive Layouts</li> 
      <li>Physics</li> 
      <li>Symbols for creating reusable elements</li> 
      <li>Persistent Symbols for master content</li> 
      <li>Viewport actions</li> 
      <li>Advanced export</li> 
      <li>ProRes video Export</li> 
      <li>Dark interface theme</li> 
      <li>Editable timing functions</li> 
      <li>Grid system</li> 
      <li>Rearrangeable interface</li> 
      <li>Templates</li> 
      <li>Behaviors</li> 
      <li>OAM widget export</li> 
      <li>Responsive design mode in Hype Reflect</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="tumult-hype-professional-interface">Tumult Hype Professional Interface</h3> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/overview-prolayout.jpg" data-src-retina="images/overview-prolayout@2x.jpg" width="750" height="450" alt=""> </p> 
     <p>This user guide walks you through the entire product, and gives in-depth details on the workings of both Tumult Hype and Tumult Hype Professional. To help distinguish between Standard and Professional features, all documentation chapters or sections covering Professional features begin with the following label:</p> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Any chapters or sections without this label cover features available in both Tumult Hype and Tumult Hype Professional.</p> 
     <h2 id="the-tumult-hype-interface">The Tumult Hype Interface</h2> 
     <p><a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/InterfaceOverview.html" target="_blank"> <img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/InterfaceOverview.png" data-src-retina="images/InterfaceOverview@2x.png" width="690" height="563" alt=""> </a></p> 
     <p>Tumult Hype also provides numerous inspectors for manipulating the document, scenes and elements. These are discussed in depth in the <a href="#inspectors">Inspectors</a> chapter.</p> 
     <h3 id="tumult-hype-professional-interface">Tumult Hype Professional Interface</h3> 
     <p>Two features unlocked by the Tumult Hype Professional in-app purchase are the Professional Dark theme and a customizable user interface. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/OverviewProfessionalDarkandLightInterface.png" data-src-retina="images/OverviewProfessionalDarkandLightInterface@2x.png" width="700" height="316" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="the-professional-dark-and-standard-interface-themes">The Professional Dark and Standard Interface themes</h5> 
     <p>If you prefer, you can switch back to the Standard theme in Tumult Hype’s General preferences.</p> 
     <p>Click and drag the customizable view handles on the Inspector, Scene and Layouts selector, or the Timeline to arrange Tumult Hype’s as you see fit.</p> 
     <p><img src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/overview-interface-drag.png" data-src-retina="images/overview-interface-drag@2x.png" width="674" height="212"> </p> 
     <h5 id="the-customizable-view-handle">The Customizable View Handle</h5> 
     <p>As you drag a view around, Tumult Hype highlights nearby drop regions.</p> 
     <h2 id="key-terms">Key Terms</h2> 
     <p>There are seven basic key terms to learn for using Tumult Hype: Scenes, Elements, Properties, Keyframes, Animations, Timelines, and Actions. The remainder of the user guide will reference these terms, and by sticking with them you’ll be fluent when conversing with other Tumult Hype users.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefscenesscenesa"><a href="#scenes">Scenes</a></h3> 
     <p>Each&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document is composed of one or more scenes. Scenes are analogous to slides in a Keynote or PowerPoint presentation, or to cards in HyperCard. Scenes contain elements and timelines. Actions are used to transition between different scenes.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefelementselementsa"><a href="#elements">Elements</a></h3> 
     <p>Elements are the manipulatable objects in a scene. They can be shapes, text, buttons, textured buttons, images, video, HTML widgets.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefmanipulating-elementspropertiesa"><a href="#manipulating-elements">Properties</a></h3> 
     <p>Properties are the attributes which define an element’s style, positioning, and auxiliary information. Most properties are animatable. Properties are defined or changed by manipulating elements in&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s&nbsp;scene editor or by changing values in an inspector. Properties define, among many things, an element’s location, size, color, borders, or the effects applied to the element.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefkeyframeskeyframesa"><a href="#keyframes">Keyframes</a></h3> 
     <p>Keyframes define a property’s value at a specific time on a timeline.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefanimationsanimationsa"><a href="#animations/">Animations</a></h3> 
     <p>Animations change a property’s value over a period of time; they are defined by two keyframes that set the starting and ending values of the property’s animation.&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;automatically creates animations between any keyframes which have different values. Animations also have different easing effects, different rates of change, such as ease-in, ease-out, ease-in-out, instant, bounce, and linear. Furthermore, by using&nbsp;<a href="#motionpaths">motion paths</a>, elements can be animated along arbitrary complex curves.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hreftimelinestimelinesa"><a href="#timelines/">Timelines</a></h3> 
     <p>Timelines contain animations. Each scene has a Main Timeline, which is automatically started when the scene is shown. Scenes can have many timelines which can play in parallel, and actions are used to control timeline playback.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefactionsactionsa"><a href="#actions/">Actions</a></h3> 
     <p>Actions make your document interactive. Among other things, actions are used to change scenes, control timeline playback, start or stop sounds, or run custom JavaScript functions. Actions are triggered in response to user events, such as mouse clicks or tap gestures, and scene events, such as scene loading or timeline playback completion. Actions can also be placed on a timeline, to be triggered at a specific time.</p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefsymbolssymbolsa"><a href="#symbols/">Symbols</a></h3> 
     <p>Symbols are a powerful tool which let you easily reuse elements, timelines, and animations. Think of symbols as scenes within scenes: symbols contain their own elements, timelines, actions, and behaviors that can be triggered independently from the scene’s. Because editing one instance of a symbol changes all instances, symbols are also useful for sharing identical elements across multiple scenes or at different positions in the same scene. </p> 
     <h3 id="a-hrefbehaviorsbehaviorsa"><a href="#behaviors/">Behaviors</a></h3> 
     <p>Custom behaviors allow you to create your own action handlers that can be triggered like Hype’s built-in action handlers. Just like Hype’s built-in action handlers, your own behaviors can trigger a series of actions. Behaviors ensure you don’t repeat any work when creating and using complex actions.</p> 
     <h1 id="scenes">Scenes</h1> 
     <p>Scenes are a useful way to separate and organize content. They are similar to slides in a Keynote or PowerPoint presentation. Scenes contain&nbsp;<a href="#elements">elements</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="#timelines">timelines</a>.&nbsp;<a href="#actions">Actions</a>&nbsp;are used to transition between different scenes. Each scene contains a unique set of elements and timelines; modifying an element or timeline on one scene will not affect elements or timelines on other scenes.</p> 
     <h2 id="managing-scenes">Managing Scenes</h2> 
     <p>Every&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document starts with one scene by default. The Scenes menu offers a few commands for managing scenes:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>New Scene</strong>&nbsp;— Creates a new scene and selects the new scene for editing.</li> 
      <li><strong>Duplicate Scene</strong>&nbsp;— Creates an identical copy of the current scene, copying all of the current scene’s elements, timelines, and animations. To duplicate a scene using a keyboard shortcut, select option + drag on the scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>Duplicate Scene (Without Animations)</strong>&nbsp;— Creates an identical copy of the current scene, copying all of the current scene’s elements, but omitting the current scene’s timelines and animations. This command is surprisingly powerful, and is often used to compose complex animations that need to span multiple scenes. </li> 
      <li><strong>Delete Scene</strong>&nbsp;— Deletes the current scene, removing all associated elements, timelines, and animations.</li> 
      <li><strong>Go To Scene</strong>&nbsp;— Offers a submenu listing all of the document’s scenes, and choosing one of the scenes makes that the current scene for editing.</li> 
      <li><strong>Go to Layout</strong> - Offers a submenu listing all layouts in the currently selected scene. <a target="_blank" href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro/" class="profeatureinline">HYPE PRO ONLY</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Tumult Hype’s Scene Selector –&nbsp;toggled by the Show Scenes toolbar button – offers additional control over scenes. Create new scenes using the Add Scene plus button, rearrange scenes using drag-and-drop, and rename them by double-clicking their name. Finally, scenes can be copied and pasted by selecting a scene in the Scene Selector and choosing Edit &gt; Copy and then choosing Edit &gt; Paste.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ScenesSceneControlsv3pro.png" data-src-retina="images/ScenesSceneControlsv3pro@2x.png" width="360" height"397"></p> 
     <h5 id="scene-selector">Scene Selector</h5> 
     <p>By default, all scenes in a document have the same size, and choosing a different default size or changing the Width or Height values affects all scenes. To change the size of just the current scene, disable “Apply changes to all scenes” in the Scene inspector.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ScenesSceneSizePro.png" data-src-retina="images/ScenesSceneSizePro@2x.png" width="289" height="298"></p> 
     <h5 id="scene-size-controls-scene-inspector">Scene Size Controls (Scene Inspector)</h5> 
     <p>The active scene’s background color is set by the Background color well found in the Color section in the Scene inspector. To make the current document transparent and prevent all scenes from drawing their background colors, open the Document inspector and deselect the Make Background Transparent checkbox in the Options section.</p> 
     <h2 id="changing-scenes">Changing Scenes</h2> 
     <p>Actions are used to transition between different scenes.&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;affords ways to trigger actions in response to mouse events such as clicks, scene events such as timeline completion, and at specific times. All of those triggers can invoke the Jump to Scene action with one of seven different scene transitions. The&nbsp;<a href="#actions">Actions</a>&nbsp;chapter has more information about all of Tumult Hype’s action triggers and different actions, including the&nbsp;<a href="#types-of-actions">Jump to Scene</a>&nbsp;action.</p> 
     <h2 id="rulers">Rulers</h2> 
     <p>Show the scene ruler by selecting View &gt; Show Ruler, and hide it with the corresponding View &gt; Hide Ruler command. Tumult Hype&nbsp;indicates the bounds of the currently-selected elements within the ruler.</p> 
     <h2 id="guides">Guides</h2> 
     <p>Alignment guides appear and disappear as elements are moved on the scene. Guides assist in arranging elements relative to each other and the scene. By default, elements snap to nearby guides; this behavior can be disabled by disabling the Snap to Guides command in the Arrange menu.</p> 
     <p>The scene and all elements automatically define their own alignment guides. The scene’s automatic guides define its center and edges. Likewise, every element generates automatic guides for its center and edges.</p> 
     <p>Manual guides can be added to the scene by choosing View &gt; Guides &gt; Add Horizontal Guides or Add Vertical Guides. Manually-created guides can by dragged anywhere on the scene; drag them off the scene to delete them. The View &gt; Guides menu features many commands for showing, hiding, locking, copying, and pasting guides.</p> 
     <p>One very powerful feature in the View &gt; Guides menu is the Add Multiple Guides command. Choosing this command reveals a dialog from which any number of evenly-spaced guides can be created. Specify either the number of columns or rows to be created, or the pixel distance between each guide. Layout Guides make arranging content in columns or rows a snap.</p> 
     <p><img src="images/bg.png" class="center" data-src="images/ScenesLayoutGuides.jpg" data-src-retina="images/ScenesLayoutGuides@2x.jpg" width="412" height="160"></p> 
     <h5 id="layout-guides-dialog">Layout Guides Dialog</h5>
     <h2 id="grid-system">Grid System</h2> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>To help you arrange your content, Hype Pro supports layout grids. Hype Pro’s layout grids follow the spirit of the popular <a href="http://960.gs">960 Grid System</a> by letting you easily create columns and gutters to arrange content. </p> 
     <p>To create a layout grid, choose View &gt; Layout Grid &gt; Create Grid. In the Layout Grid Editor, you’ll find controls to set the width of the layout grid, define the number of columns, and set the gutter width between each column.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/scene-layoutgrid.png" data-src-retina="images/scene-layoutgrid@2x.png" width="368" height="173"> </p> 
     <p>Clicking Create Grid adds an overlay to the current scene that defines the grid’s columns and gutters. Elements snap to the grid, making it easy to arrange your content against the grid. As with user guides and smart guides, element snapping can be temporarily disabled by pressing the Command key while dragging. Likewise, snapping can be permanently disabled by disabling the Arrange &gt; Snap Elements menu item. If you want to use a grid to arrange elements but don’t want the overlay, choose Arrange &gt; Layout Grid &gt; Hide Grid; reveal the grid by then choosing Arrange &gt; Layout Grid &gt; Show Grid.</p> 
     <p>Change the current layout grid’s settings by choosing Arrange &gt; Layout Grid &gt; Edit Grid, and remove the grid by choosing Arrange &gt; Layout Grid &gt; Remove Grid.</p> 
     <h1 id="elements">Elements</h1> 
     <p>Elements are the objects in a scene. They can be shapes, text, buttons, textured buttons, images, videos, audio, or HTML widgets.</p> 
     <h2 id="text">Text</h2> 
     <p>Add text to the current scene by choosing the Insert &gt; Text menu item, by using the Elements toolbar button, or typing <code class="prettyprint">t</code>. The&nbsp;<a href="#typography-inspector">Typography inspector</a>&nbsp;allows you to change the selected element’s font, size, style, color, shadow, and spacing.</p> 
     <p>For even more styling control, you can directly edit the text element’s inner HTML by selecting the element and then choosing Edit &gt; Edit Element’s Inner HTML. In the pop-up window which appears, you can enter any HTML and see the results live. </p> 
     <p>After inserting a new text element it is selected and editable. When you are done editing press the Escape key or click outside the text element. To edit the text at a later point, simply double-click the element. By default, text fields automatically resize to accommodate text entered as you type. Manually resizing an element fixes the element at the specified size.</p> 
     <p>For information on selecting fonts or using web fonts, visit the&nbsp;<a href="#typography">Typography chapter</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="images">Images</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;supports importing a wide variety of web image formats, including JPEG, GIF, PNG, and SVG. Create image elements by choosing the Insert &gt; Image menu item, or by via the Elements toolbar button. You can also drag-and-drop images onto the scene, or copy and paste them from other applications. Finally, images can be added by dragging-and-dropping from the Media Browser or from the Resource Library (assuming the image is already stored in the current document’s Resource Library).</p> 
     <p>Images initially preserve their aspect ratio when resized. You can disable this behavior by deselecting the Constrain Proportions checkbox in the Metrics inspector. If an image’s dimensions have been changed, the image can be restored to its actual dimensions by clicking the Original Size button in the Metrics inspector. </p> 
     <p>For tips and tricks regarding SVG files, please <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/tags/svg">visit our forums</a>. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsMetricsSizing.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsMetricsSizing@2x.png" width="299" height="136"></p> 
     <h5 id="proportion-and-sizing-options-metrics-inspector">Proportion and Sizing Options (Metrics Inspector)</h5> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents appear to visitors only after all included images have been downloaded. This ensures that scene transitions and animations appear as intended. To disable preloading for individual images, open the&nbsp;<a href="#resource-library">Resource Library</a>&nbsp;and deselect the Preload checkbox for any images which should not be preloaded.</p> 
     <p>Newly created image elements scale the image as the element is resized. If you need an image to repeat horizontally and/or vertically, you can configure those options from the Element inspector’s Background section.</p> 
     <p><strong>Retina Support &amp; Image Optimization</strong>:&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;automatically optimizes images during export; images are converted to formats supported on the web and resized for optimum support on “retina” screens. For more information, read the <a href="#image-optimization">Image Optimization</a> section of the&nbsp;<a href="#preview-amp-export">Previewing &amp; Exporting chapter</a> chapter. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsImageElementBackground.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsImageElementBackground@2x.png" width="271" height="186"></p> 
     <h5 id="background-property-element-inspector">Background Property (Element Inspector)</h5>
     <h2 id="video">Video</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;embeds video using HTML’s native&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;video&gt;</code>&nbsp;tag, whenever possible. If the browser doesn’t support HTML5 video, as is the case with Internet Explorer 6 through 8, Hype falls back to the QuickTime plug-in. For information about playing and controlling video, see the&nbsp;<a href="#audio-amp-video">Audio &amp; Video</a>&nbsp;documentation chapter.</p> 
     <h2 id="audio">Audio</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;embeds audio using the web audio api. For information about playing and controlling audio, see the&nbsp;<a href="#audio-amp-video">Audio &amp; Video</a>&nbsp;documentation chapter.</p> 
     <h2 id="shapes">Shapes</h2> 
     <p>You may quickly add a Rectangle, Rounded Rectangle, or an Ellipse from the Elements toolbar item or by using the <code class="prettyprint">r</code> <code class="prettyprint">u</code> or <code class="prettyprint">o</code> keyboard shortcuts. The Rectangle element is the most foundational element in&nbsp;Tumult Hype: Rectangle elements can be customized to look and behave like almost all other elements.</p> 
     <p>Add shapes to your scene by selecting Insert &gt; Shape, or by using the Elements toolbar button.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/elementsDefaultShapes.png" data-src-retina="images/elementsDefaultShapes@2x.png" width="555" height="195"></p> 
     <h5 id="default-shapes">Default shapes</h5>
     <h2 id="buttons">Buttons</h2> 
     <p>Buttons are elements which present different appearances when the mouse hovers over them, or when they are clicked or tapped.&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers two pre-configured button types, a flat button and a textured button, in its Insert menus. Any element can be converted to a button by choosing Edit &gt; Show Button Controls. Any button element can be transformed back into a normal element by choosing Edit &gt; Clear All Button States and then choosing Edit &gt; Hide Button Controls.</p> 
     <p>When button elements are selected,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;shows a segmented control above the element to toggle between the button’s normal, hover, and pressed states. When the hover or pressed states are active, any changes made to the button — including position, size, and background images or gradients — will be applied when the element is moused over or clicked. To clear the changes made in those states, choose Edit &gt; Clear All Button States.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/buttonStates.png" data-src-retina="images/buttonStates@2x.png" width="163" height="72"></p> 
     <h5 id="button-controls">Button Controls</h5>
     <h2 id="html-widgets">HTML Widgets</h2> 
     <p>An HTML widget is used to display embedded HTML in your scene or to embed an iframe of a different web page. One use for this element is to embed a code snippet that requires its own JavaScript. Insert HTML Widgets using the Insert menu or the Elements toolbar button.</p> 
     <p>To add a Twitter widget, for example:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Insert a new HTML Widget</li> 
      <li>Open&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s Element inspector</li> 
      <li>Click the Edit Code Snippet button</li> 
      <li>Paste code obtained from&nbsp;<a href="https://dev.twitter.com/">Twitter’s developer site</a>&nbsp;into the Inner HTML popover as shown below.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/elementsHTMLWidget.jpg" data-src-retina="images/elementsHTMLWidget@2x.jpg" width="480" height="635"></p> 
     <h5 id="an-html-widget-containing-twitter-widget-code">An HTML widget containing Twitter Widget Code</h5> 
     <p>To display a webpage within the HTML widget, select Specified URL and enter the full URL (make sure to include&nbsp;http://&nbsp;or&nbsp;https://).</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/elementsHTMLWidgetSourceURL.png" data-src-retina="images/elementsHTMLWidgetSourceURL@2x.png" width="272" height="214"></p> 
     <h5 id="display-a-web-page-within-an-html-widget">Display a Web Page within an HTML widget</h5>
     <h2 id="element-properties">Element Properties</h2> 
     <p><a name="manipulating-elements"></a></p> 
     <h3 id="arrangement-distribution-and-sizing">Arrangement, Distribution and Sizing</h3> 
     <p>Elements are rearranged and resized using&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s scene editor. To assist with element arrangement,&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s scene editor provides automatic guides based on the scene’s border and other existing elements. Likewise, it assists with resizing by snapping the element to match the width or height of other elements on the scene. For further control over element positioning, learn more about <a href="#guides">guides</a> and the <a href="#grid-system">grid system</a>. </p> 
     <h3 id="rotation">Rotation</h3> 
     <p>To rotate elements along the Z-axis, select the elements and press the Command key while hovering just outside of the element bounds. The&nbsp;<img src="//tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/images/elementsRotateCursor.png" width="20">&nbsp;cursor indicates the selected element can be rotated. The Metrics inspector also has controls for rotating elements along the X-, Y-, and Z-axis.</p> 
     <p>An element’s anchor point sets the element’s Z-axis rotation origin. To move a selected element’s anchor point, press Command to reveal the anchor point crosshair icon&nbsp;<img src="images/AnchorPoint.gif" width="15px">&nbsp;and then drag the icon to a new location. The Metrics inspector offers control over the anchor point location in the Rotation Origin section.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/elements-rotation-z.png" data-src-retina="images/elements-rotation-z@2x.png" width="237" height="250"></p> 
     <h5 id="element-with-z-axis-rotation-animation-and-a-custom-anchor-point">Element with Z-axis rotation animation and a custom anchor point</h5> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
       Please note that an element’s anchor point cannot be modified if it is animated using motion paths.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Multiple elements can be moved, rotated, or resized by first drag-selecting elements on the scene and then moving or resizing one of the selected elements.</p> 
     <h2 id="color">Color</h2> 
     <p>To pick a color for a selected element, click on the color well in the appropriate inspector. Tumult Hype uses the Standard Mac OS color picker, with the addition of an Opacity slider and hexadecimal/rgba field. When reducing opacity below 100%, the hexadecimal field automatically converts to the RGBa equivalent. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsColorPickerSidebySide.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsColorPickerSidebySide@2x.png" width="560" height="520" alt=""></p> 
     <p>Both the hexadecimal and rgba fields are editable and selectable for copying and pasting from other applications. </p> 
     <p><strong>Gradients</strong>: To use a gradient as an Element background, select the Fill Style dropdown in the Element Inspector and select Gradient. Rotate your element gradient by adjusting the rotation angle value. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsColorGradient.gif" data-src-retina="images/ElementsColorGradient@2x.gif" width="269" height="149" alt="Tumult Hype Gradient"></p> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        For more information about modifying the visibility of elements, read the 
       <a href="#hiding-and-locking-elements">Hiding and Locking Elements</a> section. 
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <h3 id="scaling">Scaling</h3> 
     <p>Scale an element or a group by first making a selection, and holding Command while dragging a corner resize handle. The Scale options in the Metrics inspector provide further control over the scaling ratio, height, and width.</p> 
     <p>To scale an element in response to the width of a layout, please see the <a href="#flexible-layout">Flexible Layout</a> and <a href="#responsive-layouts">Responsive Layouts</a> chapters. Scaling is a great technique to pair with <a href="#symbols">Symbols</a> used across layouts. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsScale.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsScale@2x.png" width="280" height="98" alt="Element Scaling"></p> 
     <h5 id="scaling-options-in-the-metrics-inspector">Scaling options in the Metrics Inspector</h5> 
     <p><strong>Scaling Techniques</strong></p> 
     <p><strong>Scaling <a name="scalingtechniques"></a>several objects proportionally based on the <span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span> document’s container:</strong> </p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>First, turn on Flexible Layouts in the Element inspector for the document. Set the ‘Scale’ value for Width and Height to be 100%. </li> 
      <li>Next, select elements on your scene and add them to a group. </li> 
      <li>With your group selected, switch to the Metrics inspector and select the horizontal and vertical scaling arrows. Next, deselect any pins, and set the scaling behavior to ‘Shrink to Fit’ or ‘Expand to Fill’. Also, select ‘Zoom Contents.’</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsScaleZoom.gif" data-src-retina="images/ElementsScaleZoom@2x.gif" width="270" height="186" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="scale-options-for-scalingbr-elements-proportionally">Scale options for scaling<br> elements proportionally</h5>
     <h3 id="positioning-amp-layer-order">Positioning &amp; Layer Order</h3> 
     <p>The Arrange menu provides several different commands for arranging, distributing, and resizing elements:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Bring Forward</li> 
      <li>Bring to Front</li> 
      <li>Send Backward</li> 
      <li>Send to Back </li> 
      <li>Distribute &gt; Horizontally</li> 
      <li>Distribute &gt; Vertically</li> 
      <li>Distribute &gt; Horizontally Within Selection</li> 
      <li>Distribute &gt; Vertically Within Selection</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Left</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Center</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Right</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Top</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Middle</li> 
      <li>Align &gt; Bottom</li> 
      <li>Size &gt; Make Same Width</li> 
      <li>Size &gt; Make Same Height</li> 
      <li>Size &gt; Make Same Size</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsOrderingToolbar.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsOrderingToolbar@2x.png" width="164" height="55" alt="Ordering Elements Toolbar"></p> 
     <h5 id="ordering-toolbar-items">Ordering Toolbar Items</h5>
     <h2 id="css-filter-effects">CSS Filter Effects</h2> 
     <p>CSS Filter Effects offer control over the following effects: blur, sepia, saturate, hue, brightness, and contrast. All Filter Effects can be animated. Note that foreground effects are only supported in&nbsp;<a href="http://caniuse.com/#feat=css-filters">Chrome 18+, Safari 6+, and iOS 6+</a>, and backdrop effects are only supported in <a href="http://caniuse.com/#feat=css-backdrop-filter">iOS 9+ and Safari 9+</a>.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>Like every property, both foreground and backdrop filter effects may be animated on the timeline. </p> 
     <h3 id="foreground-css-filter-effects">Foreground CSS Filter Effects</h3> 
     <p>CSS filter effects apply adjustments to any elements using properties you may be familiar with from image editing software: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/elements-CSSFilters.png" data-src-retina="images/elements-CSSFilters@2x.png" width="271" height="252"></p> 
     <h5 id="element-inspector-css-filter-effects">Element Inspector: CSS Filter Effects</h5> 
     <p>Below are a few different filter effects applied to the same image:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsCSSFiltersExample.jpg" data-src-retina="images/ElementsCSSFiltersExample@2x.jpg" width="600" height="410" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="css-filter-effects-example">CSS Filter Effects Example</h5> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Original Image</li> 
      <li>Sepia: 56%, Saturation 1.5, Brightness 86%</li> 
      <li>Saturation: 0</li> 
      <li>Blur 5.2, Saturation 1</li> 
     </ol> 
     <h3 id="backdrop-css-filter-effects">Backdrop CSS Filter Effects</h3> 
     <p>When applying <strong>Backdrop</strong> filter effects to an element, a portion of the element underneath must be visible. To add transparency, use the color picker’s opacity slider: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsColorPicker.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsColorPicker@2x.png" width="272" height="522" alt=""></p> 
     <p>Backdrop effects are great for blurring background images to ensure foreground content jumps out: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsCSSFiltersBackdrop.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsCSSFiltersBackdrop@2x.png" width="475" height="320" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="css-filter-effects-example-backdrop">CSS Filter Effects Example (Backdrop)</h5> 
     <p>The text element above has a background color opacity of 49%, and the following backdrop filters applied: Blur 2.5px, Saturation: 2.6, Contrast .7. </p> 
     <h2 id="z-ordering">Z-Ordering&nbsp;</h2> 
     <p>The stack order of elements can be changed by choosing Bring Forward, Bring to Front, Send Backward, or Send to Back from the Arrange menu, clicking the Front or Back toolbar buttons, or by reordering elements in the Element List. You can also click and drag elements or groups in the element list and move them up or down to adjust their stack order. </p> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        Elements at the top of the layer order receive touch and mouse actions. To pass clicks or touches through elements, select them, and check ‘Ignore all pointer events’ in the Actions inspector. 
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <h2 id="identity">Identity</h2> 
     <p>The Identity inspector provides access to less common element properties, such as the alt tag, a modifiable element ID, and the display name used within&nbsp;Tumult Hype.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsIdentityButton.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsIdentityButton@2x.png" width="273" height="412" alt="Identity Inspector"></p> 
     <h5 id="the-identity-inspector-for-a-selected-button">The Identity inspector for a selected button</h5>
     <h2 id="inner-html">Inner HTML</h2> 
     <p>Elements are, at their base, HTML divs. Because of this, they can contain arbitrary HTML. Edit any element’s inner HTML of any element by choosing Edit &gt; Edit Element’s Inner HTML. This is useful for pasting your own custom HTML or CSS, or for tweaking text displayed in elements. Keep in mind that if recording is turned on, modifications to an element’s inner HTML will be animated.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsInnerHTML.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsInnerHTML@2x.png" width="352" height="312" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="editing-the-inner-html-of-a-text-box">Editing the Inner HTML of a Text Box</h5>
     <h2 id="managing-elements">Managing Elements</h2>
     <h2 id="grouping">Grouping</h2> 
     <p>Elements can be grouped by selecting one or more elements, then clicking the Group toolbar button. Grouped items appear indented under their group’s name in the Element List. Clever uses of grouping include&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/masking-elements-by-using-content-overflow-groups/1342">enables cropping or masking, rotation from a specified point, and rotation on multiple axes</a>.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Elementsgrouping.png" data-src-retina="images/Elementsgrouping.png" width="94" height="53" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="grouping-toolbar-items">Grouping Toolbar Items</h5> 
     <p>Elements can be dragged in or out of groups by rearranging elements in the Element List.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsGroupedElements.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsGroupedElements@2x.png" width="272" height="164" alt=""> </p> 
     <h5 id="a-group-in-the-element-list">A Group in the Element List</h5>
     <h2 id="duplicating">Duplicating</h2> 
     <p>There are many ways to duplicate an element: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Hold option while clicking + dragging on an element to quickly duplicate an element. </li> 
      <li>Select Edit &gt; Copy, and Edit &gt; Paste. </li> 
      <li>Select Edit &gt; Copy, and Edit &gt; Paste with Animations to retain any animations linked to that element on the currently-selected timeline. </li> 
      <li>Duplicate the scene by ctrl + clicking on the scene and selecting ‘Duplicate scene’. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="pointer-events">Pointer Events</h2> 
     <p>By default all Hype elements have pointer events set to auto. This means any element will intercept all mouse and touch events for all elements underneath it. To have an element ignore mouse and touch events check ‘Ignore all pointer events’ in the Actions Inspector under the Pointer section.</p> 
     <p>This is especially useful on group and symbol elements when you don’t want the empty space inside of a group to block events. Setting ‘Ignore all pointer events’ will not propagate to all child elements. For example a child of a group that is ignoring pointer events will still intercept mouse and touch events. You must set this property on every element that you want to ignore pointer events. Pointer events is not an animatable property. </p> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        Ignoring pointer events is 
       <a href="http://caniuse.com/#feat=pointer-events">not fully supported in IE 6-10</a>. Mouseover, mouseout, and hover actions will still be intercepted by elements set to ignore pointer events.
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <h2 id="opacity-hiding-and-locking-elements">Opacity, Hiding, and Locking Elements</h2>
     <h3 id="element-visibility-amp-locking">Element Visibility &amp; Locking</h3> 
     <p>Elements locked from the lock button in the element list cannot be selected or moved on the scene, and their properties cannot be changed in the inspector. Hidden elements are not visible on the scene and are also not exported. Multiple elements can be locked or hidden at the same time by selecting multiple elements on the scene or in the Element List and then choosing Arrange &gt; Lock or Arrange &gt; Hide. In the element list, clicking and dragging on the Lock or Visibility icons will also modify their property. </p> 
     <p>Both individual elements and groups can be locked or hidden. Any adjustment to locking or visibility on a group affects the state of elements within it.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsHidingLocking.png" data-src-retina="images/ElementsHidingLocking@2x.png" width="272" height="161" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="hidden-locked-and-unlocked--visible-elements-">Hidden, Locked, and Unlocked + Visible elements.</h5> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        There are two notions of ‘Hidden’: Setting the Display value to ‘Hidden’ for an element will set 
       <code class="prettyprint">display:none</code> on that element; this is an animatable property. Clicking the eye icon on an element in the element list will remove it from the document. 
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <p>Each element’s visibility and locking buttons support modifier keys for toggling their state en masse. If you Command-click on an element’s visibility or lock button, all other elements will match the clicked element’s state. Option-clicking will change all other elements’ state, so you can easily hide or lock all other elements. Click and drag up or down on the lock or eye icons to toggle their state quickly. </p> 
     <h3 id="opacity-amp-display">Opacity &amp; Display</h3> 
     <p>To change the opacity, (also known as the transparency) of an element, adjust the opacity slider in the Element inspector. The Display option sets the visibility of the element. When set to ‘Hidden’, the element will not appear on the scene or in export. Use the ‘display’ option during animations to instantly hide an element, and opacity animations to create fades between two opacity values.</p> 
     <p>To adjust the opacity of a color used in your document, adjust the opacity slider in when using the color picker. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ElementsManipulateDisplay.jpg" data-src-retina="images/ElementsManipulateDisplay@2x.jpg" width="411" height="276" alt="Hidden element"></p> 
     <h5 id="an-element-that-becomes-hidden-in-a-timeline">An element that becomes hidden in a Timeline</h5> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        Elements at the top of the layer order will intercept mouse or touch actions even if they have a 0% opacity. To disable this behavior, please read the 
       <a href="#pointer-events">pointer events</a> section above. 
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <h1 id="animations">Animations</h1> 
     <p>Tumult Hype uses a powerful keyframe-based animation system to give elements motion and transitions. Its recording functionality makes building animations a snap.</p> 
     <h2 id="animation-user-interface">Animation User Interface</h2> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationsOverview.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationsOverview@2x.png" width="718" height="317" alt=""></p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Animation controls (left-to-right): Jump to Start, Previous Frame, Next Frame, Play/Pause, Loop</li> 
      <li>Current time indicator; matches time cursor</li> 
      <li>Record Button</li> 
      <li>Timeline Selector Popup Menu</li> 
      <li>Time cursor</li> 
      <li>Animatable Property Popup Menu</li> 
      <li>Timing Function Popup Menu</li> 
      <li>Add Keyframe Buttons</li> 
      <li>Time scale zoom slider</li> 
      <li>Timeline View with Animation</li> 
      <li>Timeline Action</li> 
      <li>Motion Path Toggle Button</li> 
     </ol> 
     <h2 id="keyframes">Keyframes</h2> 
     <p>Keyframes specify the value for a property at a specific point in time, and animations are composed of two keyframes which define the starting and ending values of a property’s animation.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationKeyframes.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationKeyframes@2x.png" width="380" height="236" alt=""> </p> 
     <p><strong>Animation Keyframes</strong> </p> 
     <p>In traditional hand-drawn animation, creating frames is split between two groups of people: keyframe artists and in-betweeners. The keyframe artists would draw the most significant frames, usually where shifts in action would occur. If they were animating a bouncing ball, they might draw two frames: the top of the bounce and when the ball hits the ground. The in-betweener would do the more tedious work of drawing the intermediate frames to bring the ball to life.</p> 
     <p>You are the keyframe artist when using&nbsp;Tumult Hype. You can specify keyframes for element properties on the timeline andTumult Hype&nbsp;will automatically generate the in-between frames for you.</p> 
     <h2 id="recording">Recording</h2> 
     <p>Recording is an intuitive way to automatically generate keyframes when creating animations. Simply click the Record button, move the time cursor, and manipulate elements on the scene or change properties in the inspector. In response to your actions,Tumult Hype&nbsp;creates the necessary keyframes on the current timeline. Recording eliminates the need to manually insert keyframes.</p> 
     <p>Create an animation of an element moving over three seconds by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Click the Record button to turn on recording</li> 
      <li>Select an element to animate</li> 
      <li>Move the time cursor to the right and stop at the 3 second tick mark</li> 
      <li>Drag an element to a new location, or resize an element.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Notice a red animation bar was created on the timeline. The red animation bar may be moved to change the start and end time of the animation. Click and drag the beginning or ending point of this bar to adjust an animations' timing.</p> 
     <h3 id="thecapo">The&nbsp;Capo</h3> 
     <p>The&nbsp;Capo&nbsp;pairs with&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s recording feature to let you quickly build animations which start and end at arbitrary times without manually inserting keyframes. With the Record button on, you’ll see a small tab — the Capo — appear at the left edge of the time scale area.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationCapo_1.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationCapo_1@2x.png" width="436" height="182" alt=""> </p> 
     <h5 id="the-capotab">The Capo&nbsp;Tab</h5> 
     <p>The position of the&nbsp;Capo&nbsp;sets the starting time for your animation. The Capo and time cursor are typically moved independently from each other, and you can adjust the position of both simultaneously by holding the control button while dragging either.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationCapo_2.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationCapo_2@2x.png" width="517" height="342" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="an-animation-created-using-recording-and-thecapo--1-animation-starting-time-defined-by-the-capo--2-animation-ending-time-defined-by-time-cursor-">An Animation Created Using Recording and the&nbsp;Capo. 1) Animation Starting time defined by the Capo. 2) Animation Ending time (Defined by Time Cursor).</h5> 
     <p>Recording and the&nbsp;Capo&nbsp;are incredibly powerful animation tools. With them in your arsenal, you’ll rarely need to manually insert keyframes for individual properties.</p> 
     <h2 id="manually-editing-keyframes">Manually Editing Keyframes</h2>
     <h3 id="adding-keyframes">Adding Keyframes</h3> 
     <p>Keyframes operate on specific properties. An animation requires two keyframes: a starting keyframe and an ending keyframe. The in-between frames are automatically formed and will smoothly transition the property value from the start to the end.</p> 
     <p>To add a starting keyframe, select an element in the scene editor. Your selected element will also appear highlighted in the element list below the scene area. In the property list below the element, you can select a specific property that you want to animate. For example, if you wanted an object to fade in, you would select the opacity property. Next, you can move the time cursor to where you want the animation to begin. Click the Add Keyframe button. This will visibly place a keyframe on the timeline. At this point, you’ll set the value of the property you want to animate. For the fade in, you would go to the Element inspector and set the opacity value to 0%.</p> 
     <p>To add the ending keyframe, move the time cursor to the point on the timeline you’d like the animation to end at. Click the Add Keyframe button again to create a second keyframe on the timeline. Finally, you’ll want to set the property to its ending value. To complete the fade in, set the opacity to 100%. A bar between the keyframes will appear; this indicates the property is animating.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationsAddKeyFrameButtons.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationsAddKeyFrameButtons@2x.png" width="277" height="276" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="per-property-add-keyframe-buttons">Per-Property Add Keyframe Buttons</h5> 
     <p>By default, clicking a property’s Add Keyframe button adds a keyframe for the associated property at the time cursor’s current time. Option-clicking the Add Keyframe button adds keyframes for all visible properties in the properties list.</p> 
     <h3 id="setting-keyframes-on-any-property">Setting Keyframes on Any Property</h3> 
     <p>By default, when you click on an element in the element list the only properties that are shown in the properties list are the opacity, origin, and size. These are the properties you’ll likely be manipulating, but&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;is capable of animating most properties you can set in the inspector. To manually add keyframes for other properties, you’ll need to add them to the currently selected element’s property list. To do this, click on the Properties pop-down menu and select which property you’d like to animate. Now this property can be selected for adding keyframes.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationKeyframesList.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationKeyframesList@2x.png" width="314" height="252" alt="Animation Keyframes List"></p> 
     <h5 id="animation-keyframes">Animation Keyframes</h5> 
     <p>If you are recording,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;automatically adds properties to the properties list as you manipulate elements on the scene or change values in the inspector.</p> 
     <h3 id="modifying-properties">Modifying Properties</h3> 
     <p>For manipulating properties with keyframes, there are two rules to note:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>If the time cursor is on a keyframe for a property and that property is manipulated through the inspector, the keyframe value itself will change.</li> 
      <li>If the time cursor is not directly on a keyframe for a property that has keyframes, and the property is changed, then the keyframes will all be offset.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Animation-On-andOffKeyframe.png" data-src-retina="images/Animation-On-andOffKeyframe@2x.png" width="459" height="198" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="time-cursor-on-keyframe--time-cursor-off-keyframe">Time Cursor On Keyframe | Time Cursor Off Keyframe</h5> 
     <p>These rules are best illustrated by considering an example involving an animation of an element’s Origin (Left) property. The animation is defined by two keyframes:&nbsp;one placed at the 1 second mark with a value of 10px, and a second at the 2 second mark with a value of 20px. With those keyframes, the animation will start at 1 second and, over a full second, will move the element to the right by 10 pixels until it reaches the ending keyframe’s value of 20px.</p> 
     <p>With this animation, placing the time cursor at either 1 second or 2 seconds will allow you to modify the value of those two Origin (Left) keyframes; any changes made to the element’s Origin (Left) value when the time cursor is over those keyframes will change the value of those keyframes and thus change the distance the element will move. Conversely, when the time cursor is at any other time on the timeline, changing the element’s Origin (Left) property will change the location of the element itself; the starting and ending points of the animation will change, but the actual animation itself is unchanged.</p> 
     <h3 id="manipulating-keyframes">Manipulating Keyframes</h3> 
     <p>Keyframes support most standard manipulations; multiple keyframes can be selected, dragged to move, copied, and pasted. While keyframes are represented by diamonds in the property area, the duration and span of animations are represented by the bars between keyframes. To the right of the elements are animation overview bars, which represent keyframes as white lines. These bars can be resized and dragged to adjust animations. They can also be multiply selected, copied and pasted, just as with keyframes.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationBars.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationBars@2x.png" width="449" height="86" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="animation-overview-bar-and-keyframe-indicators">Animation Overview Bar and Keyframe indicators</h5> 
     <p>By default, the playhead, keyframes, and animations snap to second markers and other keyframes when dragged. Disable this behavior by deselecting the Animation &gt; Snap to Seconds or Animation &gt; Snap to Keyframes menu items.</p> 
     <p>Delete both keyframes and animations by drag selecting them in the timeline view and then pressing Delete. When adjacent keyframes are deleted, the animation between those keyframes is also deleted. Deleting an element-level animation overview bar will delete all associated property animations.</p> 
     <h3 id="copying-and-pasting-animations">Copying and Pasting Animations</h3> 
     <p>To duplicate an element and its animations, first select the element on the scene or in the element list, then select Edit &gt; Copy, and finally select Edit &gt; Paste with Animations. Keyframes and animations can also be copied from and pasted to the timeline.</p> 
     <h2 id="motion-paths">Motion Paths</h2> 
     <p>Elements can be animated along complex and arbitrary curves using motion paths.</p> 
     <h3 id="creating-a-motion-path">Creating a Motion Path</h3> 
     <p>A motion path is a curved animation between two or more points. Create a motion path by first creating a basic animation between two points.</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Click the Record button to turn on recording.</li> 
      <li>Advance the time cursor to your animation’s desired ending time.</li> 
      <li>Move the element to the desired ending location.</li> 
      <li>Turn off recording by once again clicking the Record button.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Now that there’s an animation, convert the basic path to a motion path by first clicking on the animation’s path to select it for editing, and then clicking once again to add a motion path control point. Dragging the control point or the control handles alters the curve, and additional control points can be added anywhere on the path by clicking the path.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Animation-MotionPath.gif" data-src-retina="images/Animation-MotionPath.gif" width="228" height="148" alt="Creating a Motion Path"></p> 
     <h5 id="creating-a-motion-path-by-clicking-on-an-animation-path">Creating a Motion Path by clicking on an Animation Path</h5> 
     <p>Motion paths unify Origin (Top) and Origin (Left) properties under one single Origin (Motion Path) property, because the motion path itself controls the top and left position of the element. As a result,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;warns you if you attempt to convert a linear animation with different timing functions for Origin (Top) and Origin (Left), because the new motion path can only support one timing function.</p> 
     <p>Furthermore, converting an element to use motion paths will change all of that element’s animations on all timelines to use motion paths. To preserve standard animations in different timelines, create a copy of your element by selecting your element and choosing Edit &gt; Copy and then choosing Edit &gt; Paste with Animations.</p> 
     <p>By default, elements move along motion paths without rotating. When the ‘Rotation follows motion path’ option in the Metrics inspector is enabled, elements instead rotate so they’re always perpendicular with respect to their motion path with their right edge forward. If your right edge is not the “front” of the image you may need to rotate your element on the Z axis so that the correct edge is on the right side. For example if your object is moving from right to left you will likely need to rotate your image by 180 degrees.</p> 
     <h3 id="adjusting-a-motion-path">Adjusting a Motion Path</h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Shape:</strong>&nbsp;To adjust a motion path’s curve, click once on the path and then click and drag any control point to change it’s location, or any control handles to change the nature of the curve.</li> 
      <li><strong>Adding and Removing Control Points:</strong>&nbsp;Add control points by first selecting a path; once a path is selected, clicking anywhere on the path will add a control point. This cursor indicates a control point will be added when the path is clicked:&nbsp;<img src="images/MotionPathsaddcontrolpoint.gif" data-src-2x="images/MotionPathsaddcontrolpoint.gif" width="20px">.&nbsp;<br> Any control point can be removed by clicking on the control point and then pressing Delete. Because the starting and ending control points define the element’s animation, those can only be deleted by deleting the animation itself as is described in the Manipulating Keyframes section.</li> 
      <li><strong>Rotation:</strong>&nbsp;By default, elements move along motion paths without rotating. When the “Rotation follows motion path” option in the Metrics inspector is enabled, elements instead rotate so they’re always perpendicular with respect to their motion path.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>For more precise control over Motion Paths, view available&nbsp;<a href="#keyboard-shortcuts">keyboard shortcuts.</a></p> 
     <h2 id="easing-amp-animation-timing-functions">Easing &amp; Animation Timing Functions</h2> 
     <p>By default, animations use the Ease In Ease Out timing function. Ease-in-out smooths the beginning and ending movements of an animation so that changes slowly accelerate and then decelerate. To change an animation’s easing, click the animation bar between any two keyframes, then choose a different timing function from the Easing menu on the right side of the Timeline view. You can also double-click any animation bar to reveal an animation pop-up which features the same Easing menu.</p> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;supports the following animation timing functions:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Instant</strong>&nbsp;– The property jumps to the value of the ending keyframe, at the time of the ending keyframe.</li> 
      <li><strong>Linear</strong>&nbsp;– Constant steady change between the starting and ending keyframe values. </li> 
      <li><strong>Ease In</strong>&nbsp;– Constantly accelerates from the starting keyframe value towards the ending keyframe value.</li> 
      <li><strong>Ease Out</strong>&nbsp;– Constantly decelerates from the starting keyframe value towards the ending keyframe value.</li> 
      <li><strong>Ease In Ease Out</strong>&nbsp;(Default) – Accelerates change during first half of the animation; decelerates change during the second half.</li> 
      <li><strong>Bounce</strong>&nbsp;– The properties quickly change towards the ending keyframe’s value, then “bounces” off that value twice. Often used for creating natural vertical bouncing animations, by applying this timing function to an animation of an element’s Top property.</li> 
      <li><strong>Back</strong> - This function slightly overshoots its target and returns. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Easily reverse or select different variants of easing transition in the easing selection popover: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Animation-EasingSelection.png" data-src-retina="images/Animation-EasingSelection@2x.png" width="566" height="431" alt=""></p> 
     <h2 id="editable-timing-functions">Editable Timing Functions</h2> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>In addition to the 24 timing functions added to Hype 3, Hype Pro lets you create your own timing functions. All of the default timing functions show the bezier path control points that define their behavior, and adding, deleting, or editing those points creates a new timing function based on the original. You can also create new timing functions from scratch by clicking the plus button in the lower left corner of the popover.</p> 
     <p>You edit timing functions just as you edit element motion paths:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Add a bezier path control point by clicking on the path.</li> 
      <li>Click and drag a control point or its corresponding handles to change the curve.</li> 
      <li>Click on a point and press Delete to remove a control point.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>All of the motion path keyboard shortcuts work while editing timing functions.</p> 
     <p><img src="images/bg.png" class="center" data-src="images/tempanimation-easing-custom-pro.png" data-src-retina="images/tempanimation-easing-custom-pro@2x.png" width="471" height="358"> </p> 
     <h5 id="custom-timing-function-editor">Custom Timing Function Editor</h5> 
     <p>As you edit a timing function, the animations you have selected will immediately use your new custom function. To save this custom function to use in other animations click Add to list. If you need to update your saved function in the future simply make your desired edits and click Update. All animations that are using your saved timing function will be updated to use your new version. </p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      Note: Drag the corners of the Custom Timing function page to enlarge it.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h1 id="timelines">Timelines</h1> 
     <p>Timelines contain animations. Each scene has at least one timeline known as the Main Timeline whose playback is started when the scene is first loaded. Scenes can have many timelines, and using actions to start, pause, or continue timelines creates rich and complex documents. </p> 
     <h2 id="managing-timelines">Managing Timelines</h2> 
     <p>There are three ways to create timelines: </p> 
     <h3 id="timeline-selector-menu">Timeline Selector Menu</h3> 
     <p>Timelines can be added via the Timeline Selector pop-down menu by clicking on the menu and choosing the New Timeline command. Newly created timelines are automatically selected for editing. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/TimelineSelectorMenu.png" data-src-retina="images/TimelineSelectorMenu@2x.png" width="320" height="110" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="timeline-selector-menu">Timeline Selector Menu</h5>
     <h3 id="action-handler-menus">Action Handler Menus</h3> 
     <p>Timelines can be created when choosing Start Timeline, Pause Timeline, Continue Timeline, or Go to Time in Timeline as an action handler. (The&nbsp;<a href="#actions">Actions chapter</a>&nbsp;has more information about&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s various action handlers.) Choosing one of those actions presents a Timeline pop-up menu, and choosing New Timeline will create a timeline. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Timelines-Actions.png" data-src-retina="images/Timelines-Actions@2x.png" width="279" height="188" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="action-handler-menus">Action Handler Menus</h5>
     <h3 id="scene-inspector39s-animation-timelines">Scene Inspector’s Animation Timelines</h3> 
     <p>Timelines can be added in the Scene Inspector’s Animation Timelines section. Click the ‘+’ button to add a new timeline. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/TimelinesListedinSceneInspector.png" data-src-retina="images/TimelinesListedinSceneInspector@2x.png" width="280" height="174" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="animation-timelines-properties-in-the-scene-inspector">Animation Timelines Properties in the Scene Inspector</h5> 
     <p>Timelines can also be removed and modified in the Animation Timelines section. Double-click on a timeline name to rename it, and click the Minus button to delete the selected timeline. To load a timeline, select it and click Show Timeline. </p> 
     <h3 id="deleting-timelines">Deleting Timelines</h3> 
     <p>Delete a timeline by selecting it in the Animation Timelines area of the Scene Inspector and clicking the ‘-’ button. </p> 
     <h3 id="duplicating-timelines">Duplicating Timelines</h3> 
     <p>Duplicate a timeline by selecting it in the Animation Timelines area of the Scene Inspector and clicking the Duplicate button.</p> 
     <h3 id="controlling-timeline-playback">Controlling Timeline Playback</h3> 
     <p>Animations on the Main Timeline run when the scene is first loaded. Additional timelines act as containers for animations that use elements in the scene, but are not to be run when first loading a scene. (It is possible to have additional timelines run when a scene is loaded: create an&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/actions/#sceneactions">On Scene Load</a>&nbsp;action handler that invokes Play Timeline for one or more alternate timelines.) Switch between different timelines by using the Timeline Selector menu. Timelines can also be controlled by the On Drag action handler at either the scene or element level. This technique is useful for giving users control over “scrubbing” timelines, or for building complex drag animations. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/TimelinesNewTimelineMenu.png" data-src-retina="images/TimelinesNewTimelineMenu@2x.png" width="313" height="144" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="timeline-selector-menu">Timeline Selector Menu</h5> 
     <p>Animations on the Main Timeline are started automatically when a scene is loaded. Actions are used to control playback of both the Main Timeline and alternate timelines. Please see the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/actions/">Actions</a>&nbsp;chapter for more information. </p> 
     <h3 id="timeline-playback-direction">Timeline Playback Direction</h3> 
     <p>Timelines may be played either forwards or backwards. By default, a timeline plays forwards and only once. To play a timeline in the opposite direction, select ‘Play in reverse‘. To start a timeline from its ending point, create a ‘Start Timeline’ action, and check ‘Play in reverse.’ To play a timeline in reverse at the end of its animation, use a timeline action to Continue Timeline and check Play in reverse as shown below: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/TimelinesPlaybackDirection.png" data-src-retina="images/TimelinesPlaybackDirection@2x.png" width="330" height="223" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="this-timeline-action-will-reverse-the-timeline-at-4-seconds-">This Timeline Action will reverse the timeline at 4 seconds.</h5> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="demo">
      <p></p> 
      <h3 id="timelines-playback-example">Timelines Playback Example</h3> 
      <p>The document below demonstrates playback of the main timeline, additional timelines, and reversed timelines within Tumult Hype. </p> 
      <p><a href="documents/Timelines-Example.html"> </a></p>
      <div class="demoimageset">
       <a href="documents/Timelines-Example.html"><img style="position:relative;" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/demo-Timelines.gif" data-src-retina="images/demo-Timelines.gif" width="640" height="240"></a>
       <a class="previewbtn" style="margin-top:-140px" href="documents/Timelines-Example.html">View Demo</a>
      </div> 
     </aside> 
     <p class="download"><a href="documents/demo_timelines.zip" class="demo download">Download demo document.</a></p>
     <p></p> 
     <h3 id="looping-timelines">Looping Timelines</h3> 
     <p>An easy way to loop timelines is to add a Timeline Action at the end of the timeline that will run a Continue Timeline action on the current timeline, with ‘Can restart timeline’ checked. If you want a timeline to oscillate (play forward and then in reverse) add a Continue Timeline action with the Play in reverse option checked at the end of the timeline. To loop this you can also add a Continue Timeline forward action at the beginning of the timeline. <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/Oil.hype.zip">This demo document</a> illustrates oscillating timelines and looped timelines. </p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      Generally it is better to use ‘Continue’ to change the direction of a timeline. Only use ‘Start in reverse’ if you want to jump to the end and play in reverse. Using Continue Timeline to change the direction will only play the actions in that action chain once unless you have ‘Can restart timeline’ checked. However if you use a Start Timeline action the timeline will complete all actions chained with this action and then start over from the end playing all actions in the chain a second time before continuing in reverse.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h2 id="absolute-and-relative-keyframes">Absolute and Relative Keyframes</h2> 
     <p>Timelines contain starting keyframes that are either absolute or relative. By default, all timelines are created with absolute starting keyframes. The difference between absolute and relative starting keyframes is subtle but important. When a timeline has absolute starting keyframes, elements animated by that timeline will have their animated properties set to the values defined by the starting keyframes when those keyframes are triggered, and will then animate to the values defined by their ending keyframes. When a timeline has relative starting keyframes, elements animated by that timeline will use their current values when the starting keyframes are triggered, and will then animate to the values set by their ending keyframes.</p> 
     <p>This difference makes timelines with absolute starting keyframes useful for effects such as looping. When looping, it’s often desirable to have elements jump back to their starting properties; when building complex animations, it can be handy to use timelines with relative starting keyframes that animate elements from their current state, whatever it may be, rather than forcing elements to a pre-defined initial state.</p> 
     <h3 id="making-a-timeline-relative-or-absolute">Making a Timeline Relative or Absolute</h3> 
     <p>Toggle whether a timeline’s first keyframes should be relative by opening the Scene inspector and selecting the Relative checkbox in that timeline’s entry in the Animation Timelines table. Absolute keyframes are always drawn with a diamond, while relative keyframes are drawn as a circle.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/TimelinesListedinSceneInspector.png" data-src-retina="images/TimelinesListedinSceneInspector@2x.png" width="280" height="174" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="animation-timelines-in-the-scene-inspector">Animation Timelines in the Scene Inspector</h5> 
     <p>Because relative keyframes take the element’s property’s current value when the timeline is started, there are some situations where&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;cannot definitively indicate whether an animation will happen. In the example below, the Move Soccerball timeline is active and uses relative keyframes. Because the Origin (Left) animation has different starting and ending values,Tumult Hype&nbsp;knows that animation will always take place. The Origin (Top) animation, however, has the same starting and ending values. As such, that animation will only happen if the element is currently at a different Origin (Top) value when the timeline is started. Because of this uncertainty,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;draws the Origin (Top) animation bar slightly transparent, indicating that the Origin (Top) animation between the starting relative keyframe and ending absolute keyframe may not have any effect on the scene.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AnimationPotentialKeyframes.png" data-src-retina="images/AnimationPotentialKeyframes@2x.png" width="253" height="324" alt=""> </p> 
     <h5 id="potential-animation-with-relative-keyframes">Potential Animation With Relative Keyframes</h5>
     <h3 id="relative-keyframes-example">Relative Keyframes Example</h3> 
     <p>Because relative keyframes take into account the position of elements on other timelines, they can be taken advantage of to create smooth animations that animate elements across timelines. (<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/Timelines-Relative-Timelines.hype.zip">This demo document</a>) shows this technique in action.</p> 
     <h1 id="actions">Actions</h1> 
     <p>Scenes, timelines, and animations are the foundation of all&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents. Actions link together this foundation and make documents interactive. Actions are triggered five different ways:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>In response to mouse or touch events.</li> 
      <li>In response to scene events.</li> 
      <li>In response to keyboard events.</li>
