      <li>At specific times on a timeline.</li> 
      <li>Via JavaScript.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>This chapter will discuss the first three triggers, as well as the types of actions and action chaining.&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s JavaScript API is discussed in the&nbsp;<a href="#javascript">JavaScript</a>&nbsp;chapter.</p> 
     <h2 id="mouse-and-touch-actions">Mouse and Touch Actions</h2> 
     <p>Any element can respond to both mouse and touch actions. Set an action on an element by selecting the element, opening the Actions inspector, and then clicking the Plus button next to any action handler. If Use Touch Events is enabled in the Document inspector, events are mapped to the tap action in parenthesis. The following six actions can be detected:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Mouse Click (Tap)</strong>&nbsp;— A complete click (a mouse down followed by mouse up) has been completed.</li> 
      <li><strong>Mouse Down (Touch Start)</strong>&nbsp;— Once the pointing device has been depressed on the element.</li> 
      <li><strong>Mouse Up (Touch End)</strong>&nbsp;— The mouse button has been released after being pressed.</li> 
      <li><strong>Mouse Over</strong>&nbsp;— The cursor has entered the bounds of the element.</li> 
      <li><strong>Mouse Out</strong>&nbsp;— The cursor is no longer within the bounds of the element.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Drag</strong>&nbsp;— A drag has begun on the indicated element. 
       <ul> 
        <li><strong>Control Element Position —</strong>&nbsp;Controls the position of the element when dragged.</li> 
        <li><strong>Control Timeline —&nbsp;</strong>Horizontally or vertically dragging across the selected element controls playback of the selected timeline. The axis dropdown defines whether a horizontal or vertical drag controls the timeline. The direction dropdown defines whether the indicated timeline plays forwards or backwards. Use the ‘Speed’ setting to define how a gesture translates to playback speed. Select ‘Continue after drag’ to maintain the momentum of the timeline’s playback after releasing.</li> 
        <li>For deeper control over dragged elements, see the&nbsp;<a href="#dragapi">JavaScript Drag API section</a>&nbsp;of the documentation.</li> 
       </ul></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsDragPanel.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsDragPanel@2x.png" width="272" height="163" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="on-drag-action-to-control-a-timeline">On Drag Action to Control a Timeline</h5> 
     <p>Most mouse actions translate logically to touch actions. For example, tapping an element invokes that element’s touchstart action. For more information about touch support, please see the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/mobile/">Touch &amp; Mobile</a>&nbsp;chapter. By default, a tap on a mobile device will be triggered at the start of a&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>touchstart&nbsp;event. To change this behavior, disable Use touch Events in the Document inspector.</p> 
     <p>To correctly trigger mouse actions, elements must not have other elements above them or overlapping with them.</p> 
     <p>Set an action on a button by selecting the button, activating the Mouse Action inspector, and then clicking the Plus button next to the On Mouse Click action header:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsButtonMouse.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsButtonMouse@2x.png" width="464" height="294" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="a-mouse-action-set-on-a-button">A Mouse Action Set on a Button</h5>
     <h2 id="viewport-actions">Viewport Actions</h2> 
     <p>Viewport actions are commonly used to delay starting an animation until an element is scrolled into view, or to reset an animation when an element is scrolled out of view.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>On Enter Viewport</strong>&nbsp;— This element has scrolled vertically into the viewport.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Exit Viewport</strong>&nbsp;— The element has scrolled vertically out of the viewport.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>These actions will fire each time the element scrolls into or out of view. If the element is visible when the page loads, the action will fire immediately after the On Scene Load action.</p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
       Note: If your document is in an iFrame these actions will fire as you scroll the 
      <em>iFrame</em>, not the main frame. If your iFrame is not scrollable and the element is visible when the iFrame loads, the action will fire immediately, even if the iFrame itself is not currently visible in the browser. 
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h2 id="scene-actions">Scene Actions</h2> 
     <p>Scene actions trigger in response to scene events and are useful for scene-specific interactivity. The following scene actions can be triggered:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>On Scene Load</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when entering the scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Scene Unload</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when leaving the scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Layout Load</strong> - Triggered when the currently-selected layout loads. <a target="_blank" href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro/" class="profeatureinline">HYPE PRO ONLY</a></li> 
      <li><strong>On Layout Unload</strong> - Triggered when the currently-selected layout unloads. <a target="_blank" href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro/" class="profeatureinline">HYPE PRO ONLY</a><br></li> 
      <li><strong>On Key Press</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when a character key has been pressed and released.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Key Down</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when pressing a keyboard key.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Key Up</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when a keyboard key has been released.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Swipe Left</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when the scene is swiped from right to left.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Swipe Right</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when the scene is swiped from left to right.</li> 
      <li><strong>On On Swipe Up</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when the scene is swiped from bottom to top.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Swipe Down</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when the scene is swiped from top to bottom.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Drag</strong>&nbsp;— Triggered when the scene area is dragged. 
       <ul> 
        <li><strong>Control Timeline —&nbsp;</strong>Horizontally or vertically dragging across the scene controls playback of the selected timeline.</li> 
        <li>For deeper control over dragged elements, see the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/javascript/#dragapi">JavaScript Drag API section</a>&nbsp;of the documentation.</li> 
       </ul></li> 
      <li><strong>Custom Behaviors</strong> - A Custom Behavior is a reusable set of instructions which can be triggered from an action on the scene. View the <a href="#behaviors">Behaviors</a> section for more information. <a target="_blank" href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro/" class="profeatureinline">HYPE PRO ONLY</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="timeline-actions">Timeline Actions</h2> 
     <p>Timeline actions fire at a certain point in a timeline. Add a new timeline action at the playhead’s current position by clicking the Plus button in the Timeline Actions gutter, or by double clicking anywhere on the Timeline Actions’ timeline. Existing Timeline Actions can be edited by double clicking on their associated keyframe. For further control over actions beyond Timeline Actions, please see the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/javascript/">JavaScript API documentation</a>.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsTimelineActions.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsTimelineActions@2x.png" width="415" height="128" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="timeline-actions">Timeline Actions</h5> 
     <p>Edit an existing Timeline Action by double clicking on its associated keyframe to open the Timeline Action pop-up window:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsEditTimelineAction.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsEditTimelineAction@2x.png" width="342" height="226" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="timeline-actions-pop-up-window">Timeline Actions Pop-up Window</h5>
     <h3 id="example-timeline-actions">Example Timeline Actions</h3> 
     <p>Here are a few examples of what Timeline Actions can be used for:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Looping an animation</strong>&nbsp;— To loop an animation, you can set a timeline action to either Start Timeline or Go to Time in Timeline for the same timeline.</li> 
      <li><strong>Jumping to a scene or running an alternate timeline</strong>&nbsp;— Create interactivity that navigates to specific points in scenes and timelines. You would create multiple animations on one timeline, and use the Pause and Continue actions to move between them.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/2.0/actions/timelineactions.hype.zip">Download an example document demonstrating Timeline Actions</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="types-of-actions">Types of Actions</h2> 
     <p>The types of actions possible for scene, mouse, or time-based events are the same. The action menu throughout&nbsp;Tumult Hype provides quick access to eight different actions and one command.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsAvailableActions.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsAvailableActions@2x.png" width="275" height="430" alt=""> </p> 
     <h5 id="available-actions">Available Actions</h5> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Jump to Scene</strong>&nbsp;— Change to the previous, next, or arbitrarily specified scene, using one of the following seven scene transitions:</li> 
      <li>Instant</li> 
      <li>Crossfade</li> 
      <li>Swap</li> 
      <li>Push (Left to Right)</li> 
      <li>Push (Right to Left)</li> 
      <li>Push (Bottom to Top)</li> 
      <li>Push (Top to Bottom)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Note: The Swap transition is only shown in WebKit-based browsers, Firefox, and Internet Explorer 10. <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/demodocuments/scenes-transitions.hype.zip">Download this document</a> to see a demo of all scene transitions.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Run JavaScript</strong>&nbsp;— Invokes a JavaScript function. See the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/javascript/">JavaScript</a>&nbsp;chapter to learn more about what’s possible with JavaScript in&nbsp;Tumult Hype.</li> 
      <li><strong>Go to URL</strong>&nbsp;— Loads a URL.</li> 
      <li><strong>Compose Email</strong>&nbsp;— Composes an email, with optional subject line and body fields.</li> 
      <li><strong>Play Sound</strong>&nbsp;— Starts the selected sound.</li> 
      <li><strong>Stop Sound</strong>&nbsp;— Stops the selected sound.</li> 
      <li><strong>Start Timeline</strong>&nbsp;— Start playback of any timeline in the current scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>Pause Timeline</strong>&nbsp;— Pause playback of any timeline in the current scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>Continue Timeline</strong>&nbsp;— Resume playback of any timeline in the current scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>Go to Time in Timeline</strong>&nbsp;— Jump to a specified time in any timeline in the current scene.</li> 
      <li><strong>Remove</strong>&nbsp;— Removes the associated action.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="chaining-actions">Chaining Actions</h2> 
     <p>More than one action can be triggered in response to an event. For example, a button click could sequentially perform these two actions:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Go to Time in Timeline</li> 
      <li>Continue Timeline</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Clicking the Plus button in any action handler’s section appends a new action to the end of the action chain.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ActionsChaining.png" data-src-retina="images/ActionsChaining@2x.png" width="272" height="227" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="adding-actions">Adding Actions</h5> 
     <h1 id="symbols">Symbols</h1> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Symbols are a powerful tool which let you easily reuse elements, timelines, and animations. Think of symbols as scenes within scenes: symbols contain their own elements, timelines, actions, and behaviors that can be triggered independently from the scene’s. Because editing one instance of a symbol changes all instances, symbols are also useful for sharing identical elements across multiple scenes or at different positions in the same scene.</p> 
     <p>Symbols can be created either through the Symbol menu or the Symbols toolbar button. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/symbol-toolbar-button.png" data-src-retina="images/symbol-toolbar-button@2x.png" width="995" height="200"> </p> 
     <p>The New Symbol and New Persistent Symbol items create empty symbols ready for you to dive in and edit, while the New Symbol from Selection and New Persistent Symbol from Selection items take your currently selected items and all of their associated timelines, animations, and behaviors and place them in a new symbol.</p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      Note: Creating a symbol from selected elements will not move any Timeline Actions.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h2 id="standard-symbols">Standard Symbols</h2> 
     <p>Standard symbols can have multiple instances in a scene, and exist within the scene itself just as normal elements do. Copying and pasting a symbol creates a new instance of the symbol that is identical to the original symbol. In fact, editing any copy of a symbol will edit all instances of that symbol.</p> 
     <h2 id="persistent-symbols">Persistent Symbols</h2> 
     <p>Persistent symbols exist outside of scenes at the document level. They are not destroyed when scenes change, and can even be displayed and animated during a scene transition. Because of this each scene can have only one instance of each persistent symbol. Persistent symbols are fantastic for creating things like menus or master elements that shouldn’t reset when scenes are loaded or unloaded and need to always be visible.</p> 
     <h2 id="editing-symbols">Editing Symbols</h2> 
     <p>Edit any symbol by double clicking on the symbol in the scene editor or in the element list. When you enter a symbol for editing, the symbol path bar appears:</p> 
     <p><img src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/symbol-bar.png" data-src-retina="images/symbol-bar@2x.png" width="764" height="154"> </p> 
     <p>As symbols can themselves contain symbols, you sometimes find yourself diving deep into the hierarchy. The symbol path bar both tells you which symbols you’re editing and helps you navigate the hierarchy. Click on any symbol on the path to jump up to its level and click the Close button on the far left to stop editing all symbols and return back to the scene’s level.</p> 
     <p>The Symbol menu also has commands with keyboard shortcuts (Option-Command-Up Arrow and Option-Command-Down Arrow) for navigating a symbol’s hierarchy.</p> 
     <p><strong>Scaling Symbols</strong>: Symbols can be scaled like any element. Select your symbol, and hold command while dragging on the symbol’s resize handle. When scaling a standard symbol, it will not affect its scale on other scenes. Scaling a persistent symbol scales it on all scenes. Read more about <a href="#scaling">scaling</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="symbol-inspector">Symbol Inspector</h2> 
     <p>Symbols have their own inspector for settings, timelines, and symbol level action handlers (symbol load, swipe, drag, etc). It is hidden by default, but when you enter a symbol to edit it the Symbol Inspector replaces the Scene Inspector.</p> 
     <h2 id="managing-symbols">Managing Symbols</h2> 
     <p>Just like images, videos, and other resources, symbols are managed in the Resource Library.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/SymbolsResourceLibrary.png" data-src-retina="images/SymbolsResourceLibrary@2x.png" width="276" height="252" alt=""></p> 
     <p>By default deleting the last instance of a symbol in your Document will also remove it from the Resource Library. To change this behavior select the symbol in the Resource Library and uncheck “Remove when no longer referenced”.</p> 
     <p>Deleting a symbol from the Resource Library removes all instances of it from the document. When selected, symbols can be duplicated using the Duplicate Symbol button presented at the bottom of the Resource Library. The Symbol menu also has commands for deleting and duplicating symbols.</p> 
     <h2 id="playing-symbol-timelines">Playing Symbol Timelines</h2> 
     <p>Just like scenes, symbol’s can have multiple timelines. There are five ways to kick off a symbol’s timeline.</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li><strong>Symbol Timeline Actions</strong>: When a symbol element is selected, a new property called Symbol Actions appears in the timeline. These work just like timeline actions, but can control timelines inside of the selected symbol. You can use symbol actions to play, pause, go to time, and continue symbol timelines. When you use symbol actions, animations inside of the symbol will play in Hype along with animations outside. <br> <img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/SymbolSelectedSymbolAction.png" data-src-retina="images/SymbolSelectedSymbolAction@2x.png" width="431" height="305" alt=""> </li> 
      <li><strong>Action Handlers on the symbol element</strong>: When a symbol element is selected, the symbol’s timelines will show up in the element actions (mouse click, mouse over, etc) in addition to the scene level timelines.<br><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/SymbolsActionsWhenSelected.png" data-src-retina="images/SymbolsActionsWhenSelected@2x.png" width="272" height="392" alt=""></li> 
      <li><strong>Behaviors</strong>: Behaviors are a great way to control multiple symbols at once. See the <a href="#behaviors">behaviors</a> section for more information.</li> 
      <li><strong>On Symbol Load action</strong>: You can use the On Symbol Load action in the Symbol Inspector to kick off timelines the first time the symbol is shown. This is a great place to start timelines on a persistent symbol.</li> 
      <li><strong>Symbol Instance API Functions</strong>: Visit the <a href="#symbol-instances">Symbol Instance</a> section. </li> 
     </ol> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      By default symbols will not kick off their Main Timeline. However, standard symbols are automatically given a Symbol Timeline Action to start the Main Timeline and persistent symbols are automatically given an On Scene Load start Main Timeline action.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h2 id="configuring-persistent-symbols">Configuring Persistent Symbols</h2> 
     <p>When you create a persistent symbol you can choose if you want to add it to all current scenes and layouts. If you choose to add it to all scenes the symbol will automatically be added to any new scenes as well. To disable this behavior uncheck Automatically add to new scenes in the Symbol Inspector.</p> 
     <p>By default persistent symbols are shown on top of all other elements during a scene transition. You can show persistent symbols below other elements by going to the Symbol Inspector and unchecking Display on top during scene transitions. This is useful for creating animated backgrounds.</p> 
     <h2 id="renaming-symbols">Renaming Symbols</h2> 
     <p>You can rename a symbol by double-clicking its name in the element list or the Resource Library. Changing a symbol’s name will update the name of all instances of that symbol in your document and in the Resource Library.</p> 
     <h2 id="importing-and-exporting">Importing and Exporting</h2> 
     <p>Symbols can be exported and imported for re-use in other documents via the Symbol &gt; Import Symbol and Symbol &gt; Export Symbol. Do note that symbol changes do not propagate across documents. </p> 
     <h2 id="behaviors">Behaviors</h2> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Custom behaviors allow you to create your own action handlers that can be triggered like Hype’s built-in action handlers. Just like Hype’s built-in action handlers, your own behaviors can trigger a series of actions. Behaviors ensure you don’t repeat any work when creating and using complex actions. For example, you might want to simultaneously start three timelines when a scene loads and then later start those same three timelines when the user clicks a button. Before behaviors you would have to set up those three Start Timeline actions both in an On Scene Load and an On Mouse Click action handler. Now, with behaviors, you can create one new behavior that invokes Start Timeline and have the On Scene Load and On Mouse Click action handlers run that behavior. Furthermore, if you decide to change which timelines are run, only need to make changes once for the behavior.</p> 
     <p>To create a new behavior: </p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>At the bottom of either the Scene or Action inspector, click Add New Behavior.</li> 
      <li>Give the new behavior a unique name.</li> 
      <li>Add any number of actions.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Invoke the new behavior using the Trigger Custom Behavior action.</p> 
     <p>Behaviors are particularly useful when you want to control a <a href="#Symbol">Symbol</a> from outside of the symbol, or for example, the Main Timeline of a scene when clicking an object within a symbol. For example: if you have a button (not within a symbol) that you want to run a Symbol’s main timeline when clicked, you can create a custom behavior by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Enter the Symbol (double click on it)</li> 
      <li>At the bottom of the ‘Symbol’ inspector, click ‘Add New Behavior’</li> 
      <li>Give the Custom Behavior a name</li> 
      <li>Select ‘Start Timeline…’ / ‘Main Timeline’ (This action represents the timeline of the current context: the Symbol’s Main Timeline)</li> 
      <li>Next, exit the Symbol, select your button, and ‘Trigger Custom Behavior…’ and select that Behavior you created. Likewise, you can make a custom behavior in the main scene and trigger it from within a symbol.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <h1 id="audio-amp-video">Audio &amp; Video</h1> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;supports the latest HTML5 video and audio standards, and gives you the tools to create rich multimedia documents.&nbsp;For information on browser support for various audio &amp; media formats, please read <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Supported_media_formats">Media formats supported by the HTML audio and video elements</a> on MDN. </p> 
     <h2 id="video">Video</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;embeds video using HTML’s native&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;video&gt;</code>&nbsp;tag, whenever possible. If the browser doesn’t support HTML5 video, as is the case with Internet Explorer 6 through 8, Hype falls back to the QuickTime plug-in.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AudioVideoResourceLibraryVideo@2x.png" data-src-retina="images/AudioVideoResourceLibraryVideo@2x.png" width="271" height="272"></p> 
     <h5 id="video-sources-resource-library">Video Sources (Resource Library)</h5> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AudioVideoElementInspectorVideo@2x.png" data-src-retina="images/AudioVideoElementInspectorVideo@2x.png" width="272" height="247"></p> 
     <h5 id="video-sources-and-options-element-inspector">Video Sources and Options (Element Inspector)</h5>
     <h3 id="adding-video">Adding Video</h3> 
     <p>Add video elements by choosing Insert &gt; Video, or by clicking the Insert Elements toolbar button and choosing Video. You can also drag-and-drop videos onto the scene, or copy and paste them from other applications.&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;supports importing files with .mov, .ogg, .ogv, .webm, .mp4, and .m4v extensions, though only .mov, .mp4, and .m4v files can be viewed from within&nbsp;Tumult Hype.</p> 
     <h3 id="video-format-browser-support">Video Format Browser Support</h3> 
     <p>Please see <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Supported_media_formats">this page</a> for information on browser support for the various video formats. In most cases, a single .MP4 file will suffice for broad browser support. Video added to Tumult Hype use the <code class="prettyprint">&lt;video&gt;</code> tag, which supports multiple sources for one element. Adding a single video in&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;creates a video group to which other formats may be added. To add additional video formats, select your video and click Add Video Source in the Resource Library, or select your video and add your source in the Element inspector.</p> 
     <p>To convert videos into these formats, we recommend using&nbsp;<a href="http://www.mirovideoconverter.com/">Miro Video Converter</a>. It is simple, effective, and free. Instructions on how to use this software are at&nbsp;<a href="http://diveintohtml5.info/video.html">diveintohtml5.info/video.html</a>.</p> 
     <h3 id="controlling-video">Controlling Video</h3> 
     <p>The Element inspector exposes options for the selected video: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Autoplay</strong>&nbsp;— Video will play when it is shown (see compatibility note below).</li> 
      <li><strong>Controls</strong>&nbsp;— When checked, video controls are shown.</li> 
      <li><strong>Inline (iOS)</strong> - When checked, the <code class="prettyprint">playsinline</code> attribute is added, which keeps the video from playing in the iOS video player. </li> 
      <li><strong>Loop</strong>&nbsp;— Video will loop when complete</li> 
      <li><strong>Muted (needed for iOS Autoplay)</strong>&nbsp;— Audio will not play for the video. If unchecked, a video cannot automatically play inline on iOS. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p></p>
     <aside> 
      <strong>Compatibility Notes</strong>
      <p></p> 
      <p><strong>iOS</strong>: If ‘Inline (iOS) is unchecked, video will not play in Mobile Safari without user interaction. Thus, videos played ‘On Scene Load’, ‘On Scene Unload’, or using a timeline action will not play on iPhones, iPads, or iPod touches. Use Mouse Click actions to play video on iOS when not using the 'Inline’ setting. </p> 
      <p><strong>iBooks Author</strong>: Ensure that your video files do not contain spaces or foreign characters in their filenames. </p>
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <p><strong>Video FAQs</strong></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/embedding-a-youtube-or-vimeo-video-stopping-audio-when-exiting-the-scene/1093">Embedding an external video, embedding YouTube Videos, and removing videos when leaving the scene</a>.</li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/creating-play-pause-buttons-for-video/975">How do I create custom play or pause buttons?</a></li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/adding-audio-and-video-to-your-ibooks-widget/1362">How do I place a video within an iBooks Author widget?</a></li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/embedding-a-youtube-or-vimeo-video-stopping-audio-when-exiting-the-scene/1093">How do I stop a YouTube or Vimeo video when leaving the scene?</a></li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/fixing-broken-video-audio-on-firefox-ios-and-configuring-your-server-to-correctly-serve-video-files/976">Why isn’t my video playing in Firefox?</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="audio">Audio</h2> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AudioVideoAudioResourceLibrary.png" data-src-retina="images/AudioVideoAudioResourceLibrary@2x.png" width="272" height="290" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="audio-sources-resource-manager">Audio Sources (Resource Manager)</h5> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AudioVideoAudioTimelineAction.png" data-src-retina="images/AudioVideoAudioTimelineAction@2x.png" width="308" height="333" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="audio-played-by-a-timeline-action">Audio played by a Timeline Action</h5> 
     <p>On the newest browsers,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;plays audio using the powerful Web Audio API. On less recent browsers, Hype falls back to the standard&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;audio&gt;</code> tag. On old browsers like Internet Explorer 6 through 8, Hype relies on the QuickTime plug-in.&nbsp;</p> 
     <h3 id="adding-audio">Adding Audio</h3> 
     <p>To add audio to your project, first create your file formats based on your desired <a href="#audio-browser-support">browser compatibility</a>. Most browsers will play the MP3 format. To quickly add multiple audio file formats as a single audio group, use the same filenames. For example, create: <code>whalesounds.mp3</code> and&nbsp;<code>whalesounds.ogg</code>. Dragging these files into the resource library will create an audio source group called <em>whalesounds</em>. You can also individually add audio formats by selecting the audio source group and adding missing formats.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AudioVideoAudioResourceLibrary.png" data-src-retina="images/AudioVideoAudioResourceLibrary@2x.png" width="271" height="317" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="the-audio-group-39crowd39-shown-in-the-resource-library">The Audio group ‘Crowd’ shown in the Resource Library</h5>
     <h3 id="audio-format-browser-support">Audio Format Browser Support</h3> 
     <p><a name="audio-browser-support"></a></p> 
     <p>The table below outlines MP3 &amp; Theora audio format support for major desktop and mobile browsers. Please see <a href="http://caniuse.com">caniuse.com</a> for the latest information on browser compatibility. </p> 
     <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="shortcuts" width="100%"> 
      <thead> 
       <tr> 
        <th width="20%" style="text-align:left;">Browser</th> 
        <th width="40%" style="text-align:left;">MP3 Support</th> 
        <th width="40%" style="text-align:left;">OGG Support</th> 
       </tr> 
      </thead> 
      <tbody> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Chrome</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">?</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">?</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Firefox</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mostly ?<br> <em style="font-size:80%">Windows Vista+ (2006) since Firefox 22.0, Android since Firefox 20.0, Firefox OS since Firefox 15.0, Linux since Firefox 26.0 (relies on GStreamer codecs) and OS X 10.7 (2011) since Firefox 35.</em></td>

     <p>In most cases, a single MP3 variant of your audio will suffice. For the broadest browser compatibility, we recommend supplying MP3 and OGG files for each audio group. One audio source group may contain any combination of MP3 and OGG files. We recommend converting between the various audio formats using&nbsp;<a href="http://www.mirovideoconverter.com/">Miro Video Converter</a>. For generating other audio formats, we recommend&nbsp;<a href="http://audacity.sourceforge.net/download/">Audacity</a>.</p> 
     <h3 id="controlling-audio">Controlling Audio</h3> 
     <p>Once an audio source group exists in your document, audio can be played or stopped using scene, mouse/touch, or timeline action handlers. The Play Sound and Stop Sound actions can be invoked by any action handler, and those actions let you choose from any of your document’s audio groups. When playing audio, the Loop option continuously plays the chosen audio group&nbsp;in a loop. Likewise, the Preload option controls whether the audio group’s files should be downloaded before your Hype animation begins playing. For a list of all available actions, see the&nbsp;<a href="#actions">Actions chapter</a>. Below are a few examples of how actions can control audio playback:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Start audio when a scene begins by adding an On Scene Load action handler and then choosing the Play Sound action.</li> 
      <li>Start audio after clicking or tapping an element by adding an On Mouse Click (Tap) action handler to the element, and then choosing the Play Sound action.</li> 
      <li>Start audio three seconds after the beginning of a timeline by adding timeline action to the timeline, and have the timeline action invoke Play Sound.</li> 
      <li>Stop audio when exiting a scene by adding an On Scene Unload action handler and then choosing the Stop Sound action.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>If you are interested in controlling audio with JavaScript, or referencing audio files hosted externally, please read&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/controlling-audio-advanced-techniques/953">Playing and Controlling Audio with JavaScript</a>.</p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside> 
      <strong>Compatibility Notes</strong>
      <p></p> 
      <p><strong>iOS</strong>: Audio will not play on iOS devices without user interaction. Thus, audio played ‘On Scene Load’, ‘On Scene Unload’, or using a timeline action will not play back on iPhones, iPads, or iPod touches. Use Mouse Click actions to play audio on iOS. Please see <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/playing-audio-on-scene-load/3604/2?u=daniel">this forum thread</a> for workarounds. </p> 
      <p><strong>iBooks Author</strong>: Ensure that your audio files do not contain spaces or foreign characters in their filenames.</p> 
      <p></p>
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h3 id="external-audio-amp-video-youtube-vimeo-soundcloud">External Audio &amp; Video (YouTube, Vimeo, SoundCloud)</h3> 
     <p>To embed external media such as a YouTube video or SoundCloud player, use an HTML widget. Select Insert &gt; HTML Widget, and select the Element inspector. In the HTML Widget area, click Edit Code Snippet and paste your embed code in the Inner HTML area. For more information about embedding videos, read our&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/embedding-a-youtube-or-vimeo-video-stopping-audio-when-exiting-the-scene/1093">YouTube &amp; Vimeo knowledge base article</a>.</p> 
     <p><strong>Audio FAQs</strong></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/controlling-audio-advanced-techniques/953">Controlling Audio &amp; Advanced Techniques</a></li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/sync-animations-to-video-audio/980">Sync animations to Video &amp; Audio</a>.</li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/muting-audio-or-video/1705">Muting Audio</a></li> 
      <li><a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/run-javascript-when-video-has-ended/2083/7?u=daniel">Detect when audio has ended</a> </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="deleting-media">Deleting Media</h3> 
     <p>Audio and video added to your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document appears in the Resource Library. To delete media, select it, and click the Minus button.</p> 
     <h1 id="typography">Typography</h1> 
     <p><a name="fonts" href="#" style="display:none;"></a></p> 
     <p>Text is central to almost every document, and&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers powerful tools for styling text.&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s Text inspector contains numerous options for customizing text. Change text size, styling, shadows and spacing. Hype also allows you to choose from a set of Web- or iOS-safe fonts, or to even add Web fonts from&nbsp;Google’s Font Directory, Monotype’s Fonts.com,&nbsp;or from your own curated web font collection.&nbsp;</p> 
     <h2 id="choosing-fonts">Choosing Fonts</h2> 
     <p>Changing the font for selected text is as simple as clicking a font’s name in the Text inspector. By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers a set of fonts that are considered “Web safe” and work on a broad array of browsers, as well as a set of fonts available on all iOS devices. Furthermore, you can add fonts from the diverse and free set of web fonts offered by Google’s Font Directory or licensed fonts from Monotype. You can even add your own CSS Web fonts should you have your own set of curated fonts.</p> 
     <p>Select from the Web, iOS, Google, Monotype, or Custom font family selection menu to choose different fonts.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/fontsFamily.png" data-src-retina="images/fontsFamily@2x.png" width="270" height="342"> </p> 
     <h5 id="font-family-selection">Font Family Selection</h5>
     <h2 id="adding-fonts">Adding Fonts</h2> 
     <p>In addition to the default fonts available in Hype’s Text inspector, you can add fonts to your document by choosing fonts from Google’s Web Fonts library, Monotype’s Fonts.com library, by adding code provided by a 3rd party Web font service, or by adding your own&nbsp;@font-face&nbsp;CSS styles.</p> 
     <h3 id="adding-fonts-from-googles-font-directory">Adding Fonts From Google’s Font Directory</h3> 
     <p>Google’s Font Directory contains hundreds of royalty free web fonts hosted on Google’s servers. Adding Google Web Fonts to your document is incredibly simple with&nbsp;Tumult Hype:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Choose ‘Google Fonts…’ from the ‘Add More Fonts…’ popup button in the Typography inspector.</li> 
      <li>Choose a font from the list of Google Fonts.</li> 
      <li>Choose a font weight (if applicable).</li> 
      <li>Click Add Font.</li> 
      <li>Select an element and change the font family to the added font.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>To use your newly added Google Web Font, select text or an element containing text, and then choose the font from Hype’s font list. You can filter the font list to include just Google Web Fonts by choosing Google Fonts from the filter menu above the font family listing.</p> 
     <p><img src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/FontsGoogleAddMorePane.gif" data-src-retina="images/FontsGoogleAddMorePane@2x.gif" width="700" height="550"> </p> 
     <h5 id="adding-a-google-font">Adding a Google Font</h5> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice></aside=notice></p> 
     <p><strong>iOS</strong>: Google Fonts require a network connection. If you check ‘Create offline application cache’ in the document inspector, offline users will receive a network error if they haven’t yet launched your web app. If they have launched the web app, text using Google Fonts will appear in a fallback font.</p> 
     <h3 id="adding-fonts-from-monotype">Adding Fonts From Monotype</h3> 
     <p><a href="http://monotype.com">Monotype</a> offers over 50,000 professional-level web fonts from their <a href="https://fonts.com">Fonts.com</a> library. A set of fonts are available royalty-free, but most fonts require licensing via a Fonts.com account. Monotype’s font service also allows uploading your own font kits and they will host and ensure appropriate licensing and payment.</p> 
     <p>Add Monotype fonts via these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Choose ‘Monotype Fonts…’ from the ‘Add More Fonts…’ popup button in the Typography inspector</li> 
      <li>Choose a font from the list of Monotype Fonts.</li> 
      <li>Choose a font variant (if applicable).</li> 
      <li>Click Add Font.</li> 
      <li>Select an element and change the font family to the added font.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>The default listing of fonts in a new document are all royalty free, but their entire library of licensed fonts is also available</p> 
     <p><strong>Browsing for Additional Licensed Fonts</strong></p> 
     <p>While in the Add More Fonts panel, click the ‘Browse More Fonts…’ button. This will reveal an additional sheet showing over 50,000 additional fonts along with previews and a search interface. After a font has been selected, it will appear in the Font Family list. You can then choose a variant and add the font to the Hype document.</p> 
     <p><strong>Uploading Your Own Font Kits</strong></p> 
     <p>Monotype also supports uploading your own font kits. They will be hosted on Monotype’s servers. Monotype will take care of all the licensing for you.</p> 
     <p>While in the Add More Fonts panel, click the ‘Upload…’ button. This will reveal an additional sheet allowing an upload. You may drag a font kit or click the ‘Browse for .zip…’ button to select one from the Finder. After a font has been successfully uploaded, it will appear in the Font Family list. You can then choose a variant and add the font to the Hype document.</p> 
     <p><strong>Exporting with Monotype Fonts for Licensing</strong></p> 
     <p>Many Monotype fonts must be licensed and paid for. When exporting a Hype document containing Monotype fonts, a sheet will appear which completes the publish process. You will need to login with a valid Fonts.com account to use the fonts. If you do not have an appropriate account, you can continue to export your document by clicking the ‘Export without Monotype Fonts’ button. In this case, any text using Monotype fonts will use a fallback instead.</p> 
     <p><strong>Offline usage of Monotype Fonts</strong></p> 
     <p>
      <aside=notice>
        Monotype fonts currently require an online connection to display. A fallback will be shown instead if the user is offline.
      </aside=notice></p> 
     <h3 id="third-party-services">Third Party Services</h3> 
     <p>Third party services such as Typekit can be added to the Text inspector’s Font Family list by using the Add More Fonts button in the Text inspector. Many third party libraries require a snippet of code to be placed in the&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code>…<code class="prettyprint">&lt;/head&gt;</code>&nbsp;area of your exported .html file.&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/about-fonts-text-using-typekit-google-fonts-font-awesome/952">This knowledgebase article</a>&nbsp;illustrates this process for services like Typekit and Font Awesome. The general steps are:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>In the Text inspector, click Add More Fonts.</li> 
      <li>From the Source drop down menu, choose Custom CSS.</li> 
      <li>Add a descriptive name for your font in the Display Name field.</li> 
      <li>In the CSS Font-Family field, add your CSS font-family name.</li> 
      <li>Based on instructions from your Web font provider, paste any code required into the Embedded Head HTML field.</li> 
      <li>Click Add Font. Your font is now listed in the Text inspector’s Font Family list.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p><strong>Troubleshooting:</strong>&nbsp;If your font fails to display when editing within&nbsp;Tumult Hype, you may need to add ‘localhost’ to your list of approved domains. Here are&nbsp;<a href="http://help.typekit.com/customer/portal/articles/6857-using-typekit-while-developing-locally">instructions for Typekit</a>, and&nbsp;<a href="http://fontdeck.com/support/troubleshooting">instructions for Fonts.com</a>.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>The below example shows a sample embed code for&nbsp;<a href="https://typekit.com/">Typekit</a>. </p> 
     <pre class="highlight html"><code><span class="nt">&lt;script </span><span class="na">src=</span><span class="s">"https://use.typekit.net/XXXX.js"</span><span class="nt">&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</span>
<span class="nt">&lt;script&gt;</span><span class="k">try</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="nx">Typekit</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">load</span><span class="p">({</span> <span class="na">async</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">true</span> <span class="p">});}</span><span class="k">catch</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">e</span><span class="p">){}</span><span class="nt">&lt;/script&gt;</span>
</code></pre>
     <h3 id="declaring-an-font-face-style">Declaring an @font-face style</h3> 
     <p>If you have your own custom web fonts not hosted on other services, add them to Hype by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li><p>Prepare your CSS defining your custom font face. Our CSS example below loads a set of Futura Bold font files, and links those files to the font family FuturaTOTBold, with Arial and Helvetica as fallbacks shown on the right. Make sure that you enclose your font family in <code class="prettyprint">&lt;style&gt;</code> … <code class="prettyprint">&lt;/style&gt;</code> as shown below:</p> <pre class="highlight css"><code><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nt">style</span><span class="o">&gt;</span>
    <span class="k">@font-face</span> <span class="p">{</span>
        <span class="nl">font-family</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="s2">'FuturaTOTBold'</span><span class="p">;</span>
        <span class="nl">src</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="sx">url('${resourcesFolderName}/futuratot-bol-webfont.eot?#iefix')</span> <span class="n">format</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">'embedded-opentype'</span><span class="p">),</span>
             <span class="sx">url('${resourcesFolderName}/futuratot-bol-webfont.woff')</span> <span class="n">format</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">'woff'</span><span class="p">),</span>
             <span class="sx">url('${resourcesFolderName}/futuratot-bol-webfont.ttf')</span> <span class="n">format</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">'truetype'</span><span class="p">),</span>
             <span class="sx">url('${resourcesFolderName}/futuratot-bol-webfont.svg#FuturaTOTBold')</span> <span class="n">format</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">'svg'</span><span class="p">);</span>
    <span class="p">}</span>
<span class="o">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">style</span><span class="o">&gt;</span>
</code></pre> <p>For information regarding this CSS,&nbsp;<a href="http://www.fontspring.com/blog/the-new-bulletproof-font-face-syntax">please see this article on Fontspring</a>. </p></li> 
      <li><p>Click the Resource Library toolbar icon and drag-and-drop each of the font files referenced in the CSS into the Resource Library. For the broadest compatibility, font sets should include the following formats: </p><pre>futuratot-bol-webfont.eot
futuratot-bol-webfont.woff
futuratot-bol-webfont.ttf
futuratot-bol-webfont.svg</pre><p></p></li> 
      <li><p>In the Text inspector, click Add More Fonts.</p></li> 
      <li><p>From the Source drop down menu, choose Custom CSS.</p></li> 
      <li><p>Add a descriptive name for your font in the Display Name field.</p></li> 
      <li><p>In the CSS Font-Family field, add your CSS font-family name. Font providers set this name, and typically offer fallbacks as well. For our example, the Font-Family name is&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">'FuturaTOTBold', Helvetica, Arial</code>.</p></li> 
      <li><p>Paste the CSS code prepared above into the Embedded Head HTML field.</p></li> 
      <li><p>Click Add Font. Your font is now listed in the Text inspector’s Font Family list.</p></li> 
     </ol> 
     <h2 id="copying-fonts">Copying Fonts</h2>
     <h3 id="copying-google-fonts">Copying Google Fonts</h3> 
     <p>To copy a Google Font, copy a text element that uses that font into another scene or document. When copying between documents, the Google Font name will appear in the document’s resource library and the text inspector’s ‘Google Fonts’ font menu.&nbsp;</p> 
     <h3 id="copying-custom-fonts">Copying Custom Fonts</h3> 
     <p>To copy custom fonts into another&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Select ‘Edit Head HTML’ in the document inspector and copy any custom @font-face styles used for your font.</li> 
      <li>In the other document, select ‘Add Font’ and follow the instructions from&nbsp;<a href="#third-party-services">this section</a>&nbsp;of the documentation.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <h2 id="editing-amp-removing-fonts">Editing &amp; Removing Fonts</h2> 
     <p>Custom fonts and&nbsp;Google Web Fonts&nbsp;added to your document appear in the document’s Resource Library. To edit a custom font, select it in the Resource library and click Edit Font at the bottom.</p> 
     <p>To remove a font, choose it in the Resource Library and click the Minus button. If you have added font files (e.g. .otf or .ttf files) you should also remove those from the Resource Library.</p> 
     <h1 id="physics">Physics</h1> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Physics introduces a whole new way of animating elements in Hype. Hype Pro offers you control over an element’s physical properties – bounce, friction, air drag, and density – and over the scene’s gravity. Together, those properties enable complex, dynamic animations that would be difficult to create with just a keyframe based animation system.</p> 
     <p>Due to its interactive and simulated nature, Physics-based animations can only be viewed when previewing or exporting (that is, not within Hype’s scene editor).</p> 
     <p>Hype’s physics engine is based on <a href="http://brm.io/matter-js/">Matter.js</a> by Liam Brummitt.</p> 
     <h2 id="scene-physics-gravity">Scene Physics Gravity</h2> 
     <p>Scene Physics Gravity defines the force and angle of gravity in the current scene. Lower numbers equate to a smaller gravity force, and higher numbers increase gravity. The default gravity angle (180°) and force (1.0) simulate regular Earthly gravity. To change the direction of gravity based on a device’s current orientation, enable ‘Control gravity with device tilt’.</p> 
     <div class="imagebox"> 
      <a href="images/physics-tilt.gif"><img style="clear:both;display:block;" align="right" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/physics-gravity-tilt.gif" data-src-retina="images/physics-gravity-tilt.gif" width="150"></a> 
      <br> 
      <p class="caption">Device Tilt</p> 
     </div> 
     <h3 id="symbol-physics-gravity">Symbol Physics Gravity</h3> 
     <p>To set the gravity within a symbol, select a symbol and adjust the ‘Symbol Physics Gravity’ properties in the Physics inspector. This change propagates to instances of that symbol and allows you to use multiple gravity settings in a single scene.</p> 
     <h3 id="collision-behavior">Collision Behavior</h3> 
     <p>Static and dynamic elements on the same scene collide and interact with each other. To isolate elements from colliding with other elements, add them to a symbol. Symbols define a new physics space where collisions take place.</p> 
     <h2 id="element-physics">Element Physics</h2> 
     <p>By default, new elements have no physics properties applied and are considered inactive. They don’t play any role in Hype’s physics engine. There are two additional element physics states:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Static - Interacts without Movement</strong>: Gravity does not affect static elements. Static elements are useful for creating hard edges through which dynamic elements cannot pass. </li> 
      <li><strong>Dynamic - Full Physics Body</strong>: Gravity settings for the scene affect dynamic physics bodies on scene load. These elements will collide with other dynamic bodies and static bodies on the same scene. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      Dynamic elements will not interact with other physics bodies within other symbols. Physics bodies within a symbol will likewise not interact with bodies outside of the symbol.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h3 id="physics-properties">Physics Properties</h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Density</strong>: Density is the area divided by the mass. If an element increases in size and stays the same density, its mass will therefore grow.</li> 
      <li><strong>Bounce</strong>: (Also known as restitution) Higher bounce factors will make for more elastic collisions. A bounce factor over 1.0 will add energy to the collision.</li> 
      <li><strong>Friction</strong>: determines how two bodies will slide against each other.</li> 
      <li><strong>Air Drag</strong>: The friction air provides when an object falls. A beach ball would have high air drag and a bowling ball low air drag.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="tips-and-tricks">Tips and Tricks</h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Physics is a simulation and may run differently depending on various browser and animation conditions</li> 
      <li>To simulate physics from a top-down perspective, set the scene’s gravity to 0. Then use the air drag property as friction for the surface.</li> 
      <li>To apply a force to an element, use traditional keyframe animations for the top/left properties. The timing function should generally be linear as if it were a function that eased-out the velocity would decrease and not animate as expected</li> 
      <li>To create an invisible edge through which dynamic elements cannot pass, add a rectangle to the scene, make it a ‘static’ element, and then set its opacity to 0. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><strong>The demo document below covers the following techniques in Tumult Hype Professional:</strong> </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Element Types: Static, Inactive, and Dynamic</li> 
      <li>Setting different gravity values on the same scene using Symbols</li> 
      <li>Defining dynamic element edges</li> 
      <li>Manipulating physics bodies with animations</li> 
      <li>Creating top-down physics environments</li> 
      <li>Animation easing vs. physics animations</li> 
      <li>Creating element containers</li> 
      <li>Creating collisions</li> 
      <li>Advanced Physics with animations: Using keyframes to change physics properties</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="demo">
      <p></p>

      <div class="demoimageset">
       <a href="documents/PhysicsDemo/PhysicsMaster.zip" alt="_blank"><img style="position:relative;" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/physics-castle.gif" data-src-retina="images/physics-castle.gif" width="640" height="292"></a>
       <a class="previewbtn" style="margin-top:-170px" href="documents/PhysicsDemo/PhysicsMaster.zip" alt="_blank">Download Demo</a>
      </div>

     <p></p> 
     <p><a href="documents/PhysicsDemo/PhysicsMaster.html">View demo on the web</a>.</p> 
     <h1 id="responsive-layouts">Responsive Layouts</h1> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Responsive layouts make it easy to make your document look great on every size screen. Hype allows you to create multiple layouts for a single scene which are shown at specific breakpoints. When displayed in a browser Hype will dynamically load the correct layout based on the current width of the device’s viewport.</p> 
     <p>To test your responsive layouts while previewing, we recommend using Safari’s <a href="https://developer.apple.com/safari/tools/">responsive design mode</a>. To test responsive layouts on an iOS device, use responsive preview mode in <a href="#hype-reflect">Hype Reflect</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="creating-new-layouts">Creating New Layouts</h2> 
     <p>There are two ways to create new layouts:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Reveal the layout selector by clicking the Layouts toolbar button at the top left of the Hype window, then click the + button in the layout selector’s header.</li> 
      <li>Click the Add New Layout&nbsp;button in the Scene inspector’s Responsive Layout section.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ResponsiveInitialAddLayout.png" data-src-retina="images/ResponsiveInitialAddLayout@2x.png" width="622" height="" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="targeting-the-ipad39s-portrait-orientation">Targeting the iPad’s Portrait Orientation</h5> 
     <p>The breakpoint width you specify tells Hype to display that layout at that specific width and above. Hype will continue to display that layout as the browser width grows until it hits the next layout’s breakpoint.</p> 
     <p>When you create a new layout Hype will copy all elements, animations, and timelines from one of your existing layouts which best matches the new breakpoint you created. </p> 
     <p>Any changes made to elements or animations on one layout will not affect other layouts. <a href="#symbols">Symbols</a> are a great way to share content across multiple layouts. </p> 
     <h2 id="adjusting-layouts">Adjusting Layouts</h2> 
     <p>Adjusting a layout’s dimensions will by default change the dimensions of all layouts which have the same breakpoint width. (You can see a layout’s breakpoint width in the Scene inspector’s Responsive Layout section.) For example, adjusting the height of the default iPhone layout will change the height of all layouts which also have a breakpoint width of 320px. To modify only the selected layout disable the “Apply to matching layouts” option in the Scene inspector’s Layout Size section.</p> 
     <h3 id="deleting-layouts">Deleting Layouts</h3> 
     <p>Delete a layout by Control-clicking on the layout and choosing Delete Layout from the contextual menu. </p> 
     <h3 id="renaming-layouts">Renaming Layouts</h3> 
     <p>Rename a layout by Control-clicking on the layout and choosing Rename Layout from the contextual menu, or by double clicking on the layout’s name.</p> 
     <h3 id="duplicating-layouts">Duplicating Layouts</h3> 
     <p>To copy a layout from one scene to another: </p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Select the layout.</li> 
      <li>Choose Edit &gt; Copy.</li> 
      <li>Switch to the destination scene.</li> 
      <li>Choose Edit &gt; Paste.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <h3 id="advanced-layout-configurations">Advanced Layout Configurations</h3> 
     <p>To see examples of responsive layouts in action, visit the <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/c/responsive">Responsive</a> section on the forums. </p> 
     <p>For programmatic control over layouts, view <a href="#layout-functions">Layout Functions</a>. </p> 
     <p><strong>Embedding within a responsive document</strong></p> 
     <p>To create an animation for embedding within another website, you will need to think about the mobile theme for that website, and the types of breakpoints already present in your website design. Before building all of your layouts out, embed a test document within your site to ensure that your various layouts are shown when you expect. Safari’s <a href="https://developer.apple.com/safari/tools/">Responsive Design Mode</a> is great for testing breakpoints.</p> 
     <p>A responsive Tumult Hype document expands to fit the available space of its parent element. If the container where you place your document has a maximum width of 500px, that should be your largest layout’s width. If you are embedding your document in a site with no responsive features, there’s no need to create additional layouts. </p> 
     <p><em>Note: Use only ‘width’ scaling to avoid common issues when embedding within another site. If your document scales based on both the width and height, it may not appear when embedded. When using height scaling, your document will fit the available space of the containing element. If there is no height set on that element, your animation might not appear because it will have a height of 0. For help troubleshooting this, please see <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/hype-disappears-when-scale-turned-on/4733">this thread</a>.</em></p> 
     <h1 id="flexible-layout">Flexible Layout</h1> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers a powerful layout system for resizing and scaling documents, allowing Hype animations to respond as the browser’s window or device’s viewport changes size. </p> 
     <h2 id="document-scaling">Document Scaling</h2> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;animations have a fixed width and height, and do not respond to window or viewport size changes. To make your animation responsive to size changes, you must first select the Width and Height Scale checkboxes in&nbsp;Hype’s Element inspector. Enabling these options allows your document to respond to width or height size changes as desired. The Width and Height Scale options are complimented by percentage fields which define how much of the containing window or div the Hype document should fill. The default value is 100%, which means the&nbsp;Hype&nbsp;document will expand or contract to fill the width or height of its container. Reducing this number restricts how the document will expand. For example, setting the value to 50% means the Hype document will only expand to fill half of the width or height of its container. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/FlexibleLayout-ScalingSettings.png" data-src-retina="images/FlexibleLayout-ScalingSettings@2x.png" width="272" height="205" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="document-scale-settings">Document Scale Settings</h5>
     <h2 id="element-pinning-and-sizing">Element Pinning and Sizing</h2> 
     <p>Enabling document scaling is only the first step for creating a completely responsive document. After deciding how your document should scale, you then need to define how elements in the document should adapt to size changes. This is done by “pinning” elements to edges of the scene, allowing the elements to resize horizontally or vertically, and, for proportionally sized elements like images, controlling how they should scale. Hype’s Metrics inspector offers a Flexible Layout section which contains all of the controls for managing how elements should adapt to document size changes. Please note that this section will be disabled if you have not first set scaling settings in the Document inspector. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/FlexibleLayoutAnimation.gif" width="273" height="176" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="element-scale-settings">Element Scale Settings</h5>
     <h3 id="pinning">Pinning</h3> 
     <p>Pinning an element to an edge instructs that element to move as the edge itself moves. When pinned to non-opposing edges, such as the bottom and right edge, the distance from the element to those edges remains fixed. In other words, an element that is placed 100 pixels away from the right edge and is also pinned to the right edge will change its location as the document resizes so it’s always 100 pixels away from the right edge. When an element is pinned to opposing edges, the element’s location changes so the proportion of the distance from the element’s center to the opposing edges is always preserved. The best example for this case is element centering: an element that is centered between the right and left edges and is also pinned to those edges will always be centered regardless of how the document’s size changes. A more complex example is an element in a 1000px wide document whose center is 200px from the left edge and 800px from the right edge. When this element is pinned to both edges and the document has width scaling enabled, the element’s center will always be positioned so that 20% of the document’s width is between itself and the document’s left edge while 80% of the distance is between itself and the right edge. </p> 
     <h3 id="sizing">Sizing</h3> 
     <p>Element resizing is controlled by the two sizing arrows presented in the Metric inspector’s Flexible Layouts section. By default, both sizing arrows are disabled which means that neither the element’s width nor height will change as the document’s size changes. Enabling either one or both of the arrows allows the element to change its size either horizontally or vertically. Like pinning, an element’s size changes proportionally to the document’s size. Thus, an element whose height is 20% of the document’s height will resize to ensure its height is always 20% of the document’s height. </p> 
     <h3 id="scaling-behavior">Scaling Behavior</h3> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/FlexibleLayoutScalingBehavior.png" data-src-retina="images/FlexibleLayoutScalingBehavior@2x.png" width="271" height="231" alt=""> </p> 
     <p><strong>Scaling behavior settings appear when height and width sizing is selected</strong> </p> 
     <p>The scaling behavior control allows you to change how elements should be resized. This control is only enabled when an element is allowed to resize both its width and height. When an element is allowed to resize in both dimensions, the default scaling behavior is to stretch the element. This is ideal in most situations, but there are times —&nbsp;such as when an image is being resized —&nbsp;where an element should not be arbitrarily stretched and instead its proportions should be preserved. To handle those situations, Hype offers two additional scaling behaviors which preserve the element’s aspect ratio: Shrink to Fit and Expand to Fill. When Shrink to Fit is chosen, Hype ensures that the element will never expand outside of its bounding region. Conversely, when Expand to Fill is chosen, Hype will make sure the element always fills its bounding region, even if that means it may spill outside. As an analogy, consider what happens when watching wide-screen content on a TV: viewing that content letterboxed is similar to Shrink to Fit as all of the content is always visible on the TV. Likewise, viewing the same content fullscreen is similar to Expand to Fill, as the video expands to fill the TV even though some content falls off the screen. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/scalingBehaviors1.png" data-src-retina="images/scalingBehaviors1@2x.png" width="500" height="120"></p> 
     <h5 id="stretch-distorting">Stretch (Distorting)</h5> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/scalingBehaviors2.png" data-src-retina="images/scalingBehaviors2@2x.png" width="500" height="120"></p> 
     <h5 id="shrink-to-fit-will-not-distort">Shrink to Fit (Will not distort)</h5> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/scalingBehaviors3.png" data-src-retina="images/scalingBehaviors3@2x.png" width="500" height="150"></p> 
     <h5 id="expand-to-fill-will-not-distort">Expand to Fill (Will not distort)</h5>
     <h3 id="animations">Animations</h3> 
     <p>Both standard animations and motion paths take into account the element’s sizing and pinning settings, and adapt to the element’s position and size changes as needed. </p> 
     <h3 id="viewport-settings">Viewport Settings</h3> 
     <p>Documents with a scaling turned on for the height dimension will not display vertical scrollbars. Likewise, documents with a scale percentage set on their width dimension will not display horizontal scrollbars. If small screen sizes conceal parts of your document outside of the viewport, uncheck the ‘height’ scale checkbox. To specifically address issues with hidden content on mobile devices, set the viewport width property of your document to ‘device height’. For more information on the viewport property, read the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/mobile/">Touch &amp; Mobile</a>&nbsp;chapter. </p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="demo">
      <p></p> 
      <h3 id="flexible-layouts-example">Flexible Layouts Example</h3> 
      <p>The document demonstrates scaling and pinning elements using the Flexible Layouts feature: <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/FlexibleLayouts/FlexibleLayoutExample.html" alt="_blank"> </a></p>
      <div class="demoimageset">
       <a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/FlexibleLayouts/FlexibleLayoutExample.html" alt="_blank"><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/FlexibleLayoutExampleThumb.png" data-src-retina="images/FlexibleLayoutExampleThumb@2x.png" width="598" height="448" alt=""></a>
       <a class="previewbtn" style="margin-top:-165px" href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/3.0/documents/FlexibleLayouts/FlexibleLayoutExample.html" alt="_blank">View Demo</a>
