     <h1 id="hype-reflect">Hype Reflect</h1> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/reflect/download/?utm_source=reflectdocumentation&amp;utm_medium=web&amp;utm_campaign=hype_reflect"><img style="padding-left:45px;padding-bottom:30px;" src="images/ReflectDownloadontheappstore.gif" data-src-2x="images/ReflectDownloadontheappstore.gif" width="120px" align="right"></a></p> 
     <p>Tumult Hype’s mobile gestures and web app support provide you with amazing tools to create mobile content, and&nbsp;Hype Reflect for iOS&nbsp;allows you to quickly preview your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document on any iOS device.&nbsp;<a href="http://tumult.com/hype/reflect/">Here’s a quick visual overview</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="connecting-tohype-reflect">Connecting to&nbsp;Hype Reflect</h2> 
     <p>Preview your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document in&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li><a href="https://bit.ly/HypeReflectApp">Download&nbsp;Hype Reflect</a>&nbsp;from the iOS App Store.</li> 
      <li>Make sure that your Mac and your iOS devices are connected to the same Wi-Fi network.</li> 
      <li>In&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;on your Mac, click the Preview menu in the toolbar and choose your iOS device.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Your current&nbsp;Hype&nbsp;document should appear on your iOS device, in&nbsp;Hype Reflect.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/HypeReflectPreviewDisclosure.png" data-src-retina="images/HypeReflectPreviewDisclosure@2x.png" width="378" height="254" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="preview-drop-down-intumult-hype-available-devices-highlighted-blue">Preview drop-down in&nbsp;Tumult Hype: Available devices highlighted blue</h5> 
     <p>If you close&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;on your Mac or leave your WiFi network, the preview will close in&nbsp;Hype Reflect.</p> 
     <h2 id="mirror-mode">Mirror Mode</h2> 
     <p>While in Mirror Mode,&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;instantly mirrors every single change made in&nbsp;Tumult Hype. This makes Mirror Mode a fantastic tool for designing iOS content. Enable Mirror Mode by tapping the&nbsp;<img src="images/Reflect-mirrorOff.png" data-src-2x="images/Reflect-mirrorOff.png" width="20px">&nbsp;icon.</p> 
     <h2 id="preview-mode">Preview Mode</h2> 
     <p>When you initially preview your document, your document is in Preview mode. In this mode, your document behaves almost exactly as if it were viewed in Mobile Safari itself.</p> 
     <p>Switch between different scenes within&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;by tapping the Scenes icon in the upper left hand corner and choosing your desired scene. Reload the document by tapping the reload button; this is a quick way to get most recent changes made in Tumult Hype.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/HypeReflectResponsiveIphone.png" data-src-retina="images/HypeReflectResponsiveIphone@2x.png" width="650" height="544" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="left-preview-right-preview-in-responsive-mode">Left: Preview, Right: Preview in Responsive Mode</h5>
     <h2 id="responsive-preview-mode">Responsive Preview Mode</h2> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Responsive preview mode is a great way to test <a href="#responsive-layouts">Responsive Layouts</a> and <a href="#flexible-layout">Flexible Layouts</a> in your document. Tap the responsive preview icon to enter this mode. When selected, device icons appear at the bottom of Hype Reflect for switching to smaller device widths. When selecting smaller devices, drag handles appear on either side of your document. This feature is supported when previewing from Hype Professional on an iPhone 6 or larger. Your device will allow previewing at your current resolution and smaller. Previewing on an iPad is preferable, as a wide array of iOS device widths can be tested. </p> 
     <h2 id="more-options">More Options</h2> 
     <p>While using&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;on an iPhone or iPod, you may enable the following options by tapping the icons in <span class="notranslate">Hype Reflect’s</span> top toolbar: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Open in Safari – Opens the current document within Mobile Safari.</li> 
      <li>Console – Displays any JavaScript console logs.</li> 
      <li>Fullscreen – Simulates a full screen web app. To exit fullscreen, click the icon in the lower left hand corner.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="testing-and-previewing">Testing and Previewing</h2> 
     <p>For tutorials on how to preview your document on additional platforms like Chrome on Android, and Internet Explorer running on Windows, <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/video-tutorials-testing-your-tumult-hype-documents-on-chrome-windows-ios-and-android/1381">read this forum post</a>. </p> 
     <h2 id="hype-reflect-faq">Hype Reflect FAQ</h2> 
     <p><strong>I’m unable to connect to&nbsp;Hype Reflect. What do I do?</strong></p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Make sure that your iOS device and your computer are connected to the same WIFI network.</li> 
      <li><a href="http://support.apple.com/kb/HT1430?viewlocale=en_US&amp;locale=en_US">Restart your iOS device</a>&nbsp;&amp; turn WIFI on your Mac off and on.</li> 
      <li>Open System Preferences on your Mac and open the ‘Security and Privacy’ or ‘Security’ area. In the ‘Firewall’ section, click ‘More Options’ and make sure that ‘Block all incoming connections’ is not checked. (<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/2.0/images/HypeReflectFirewall.png">View Screenshot</a>).</li> 
      <li>Make sure that firewall applications such as&nbsp;<a href="https://www.obdev.at/products/littlesnitch">Little Snitch</a>&nbsp;do not block connections requested by&nbsp;Tumult Hype. To edit blocked applications, open Little Snitch’s preferences.</li> 
      <li>Make sure that devices on your local area network can connect to other devices on your network. Your router should not be blocking connections between local devices; you may need to contact your network administrator to resolve this issue.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>If the suggestions above do not work, you can connect to&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;by creating an ad hoc network between your Mac and your iOS device&nbsp;<a href="http://support.apple.com/kb/PH10666">based on these instructions</a>. Please note this may disrupt your connection to the Internet. Please&nbsp;<a href="mailto:support+hypereflect@tumult.com">get in touch</a>&nbsp;if you continue to have issues connecting.</p> 
     <h1 id="touch-amp-mobile">Touch &amp; Mobile</h1> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers several options for producing touch-friendly interactivity for: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>iBooks Author Widgets</li> 
      <li>Animations on the web</li> 
      <li>Interactive elements within mobile applications</li> 
      <li>Animations accessible from a touch screen</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>This chapter explores initial configuration options for your document, touch actions available at the scene and element level, and offers tips for optimizing for touch screens. </p> 
     <h2 id="document-options">Document Options</h2> 
     <p>The Document inspector contains basic configuration options for your Hype document that effect how your document appears on mobile devices: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Document Size</strong>&nbsp;– When selecting a document size, choose from many different mobile device sizes in the document size drop down.</li> 
      <li><strong>Create offline application cache</strong>&nbsp;– When selected,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;generates a cache manifest file for resources used in your project. With this option selected, your document, when loaded as a web app, will download and locally save everything needed to ensure the document works even when the device is offline.&nbsp;<strong>Note:</strong>&nbsp;Your document will need to be loaded once as a web app to prime the cache. Also, Google fonts require an Internet connection as they cannot be cached on the device.</li> 
      <li><strong>Viewport</strong>&nbsp;– Choosing Document Width sets the document’s viewport to match your document’s width. Device Width and Device Height define the exported document’s viewport to match the viewing screen’s width or height. Choosing Don’t Set excludes any viewport tag from your document’s exported content.</li> 
      <li><strong>Initial Scale 1.0</strong>&nbsp;–&nbsp;Selecting this option adds the “initial-scale=1.0” property to the exported page’s viewport.</li> 
      <li><strong>Allow user scaling</strong>&nbsp;– When selected, users can pinch and zoom to zoom in to and out of your document.</li> 
      <li><strong>Use touch events</strong>&nbsp;– When selected, actions set in the Actions inspector default to tap events when possible. For example, a Mouse Click will be fired after a Tap without any delay.</li> 
      <li><strong>Show tap highlight</strong>&nbsp;– When selected, the default tap highlight color appears when tapping elements. Tap highlight does not appear when ‘Use Touch Events’ is selected.</li> 
      <li><strong>Home screen web app</strong>&nbsp;– This option allows visitors to add your web app to their iOS device’s home screen and choose a color for the status bar. To add the Apple Touch Startup images to your document,&nbsp;<a href="#appleimages">click here</a>.</li> 
      <li><strong>Status bar</strong>&nbsp;–&nbsp;If “Home screen web app” is enabled, allows you to choose the desired appearance for your web app’s status bar.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="scene-touch-actions">Scene Touch Actions</h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Scene level touch actions — such as swiping and dragging on the scene — can trigger one or more actions. Swipe actions are a great way to introduce mobile device support in your document’s navigation. For example, the following action creates a natural swiping motion between scenes. In addition to swiping up, down, left and right, you may also trigger actions from Drag events. Drag events at the scene level can control the playback of a timeline when dragging horizontally or vertically, or it may optionally trigger JavaScript. Our<a href="#dragapi">JavaScript API</a>&nbsp;offers more options for the dragging API. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="element-touch-actions">Element Touch Actions</h2> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;optimizes events that occur on touch events. For example, a tap on a link in Mobile Safari fires only after a 300ms delay, regardless of the speed of the tap. With Use Touch Events enabled in the document inspector, tap actions fire after the finger has left the surface of the screen. The tables below provide a bit more information on these events and how they behave with or without Use Touch Events. </p> 
     <h3 id="usetoucheventson"><strong>“Use Touch Events” Enabled</strong></h3> 
     <table> 
      <tbody> 
       <tr> 
        <td width="149" style="text-align:left;"><b>Action Name</b></td> 
        <td width="111" style="text-align:left;"><b>Mouse Event</b></td> 
        <td width="154" style="text-align:left;"><b>Touch Event</b></td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Click</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Click</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Tap on Element</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Down</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Down</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">`touchstart`</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Up</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Up</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">`touchend`</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Over</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Hover</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">n/a</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Out</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">End Hover</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">n/a</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Drag</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Click and Drag</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Tap and Drag</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody> 
     </table> 
     <p><strong>Scrolling &amp; Touch Events:</strong>&nbsp;The mouse click event fires after the element has been tapped. It triggers on Touch End but will cancel if a scroll begins before that occurs. If touch events are enabled, a scrolling movement that begins on an element with a Mouse Down event, the action will fire. </p> 
     <h3 id="usetoucheventson"><strong>“Use Touch Events” Disabled</strong></h3> 
     <table> 
      <thead> 
       <tr> 
        <td width="149" style="text-align:left;"><b>Action Name</b></td> 
        <td width="111" style="text-align:left;"><b>Mouse Event</b></td> 
        <td width="154" style="text-align:left;"><b>Touch Event</b></td> 
       </tr> 
      </thead> 
      <tbody> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Click</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Click</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Emulated Mouse Event +300ms delay</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Down</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Down</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Emulated Mouse Event +300ms delay</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Up</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Mouse Up</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Emulated Mouse Event +300ms delay</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Over</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Hover</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">n/a</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Mouse Out</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">End Hover</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">n/a</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">On Drag</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Click and Drag</td> 
        <td style="text-align:left;">Tap and Drag</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody> 
     </table> 
     <p>When Use Touch Events is disabled, if you begin scrolling on an element with a Mouse Down event, a Mouse Down event&nbsp;<strong>will not</strong>&nbsp;fire. For more information about touch events and emulated mouse events, please see&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.apple.com/library/ios/#documentation/AppleApplications/Reference/SafariWebContent/HandlingEvents/HandlingEvents.html">Safari Web Content Guide: Handling Events</a>. </p> 
     <h2 id="testing">Testing</h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Touch actions work on mobile and desktop browsers, but to really test how a touchable interface behaves, test on the mobile browser and device you’d like to support and host your document from a staging server. </li> 
      <li><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/reflect">Hype Reflect</a>&nbsp;is a free companion iOS app that streamlines previewing Hype documents on iOS devices. When Reflect is open on an iOS device,&nbsp;Hype Reflect&nbsp;appears as a preview option alongside Safari, Chrome, and other browsers. When previewing responsive layouts in Hype Pro on an iPad 6 or larger device, Hype Reflect’s responsive design mode lets you simulate difference device sizes.&nbsp;<a href="http://tumult.com/hype/reflect">Learn more about Hype Reflect</a>&nbsp;and visit the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/previewing/">Previewing Chapter</a>. Use&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.apple.com/library/content/documentation/AppleApplications/Conceptual/Safari_Developer_Guide/Introduction/Introduction.html">Mobile Safari’s developer tools</a>&nbsp;to profile and test actions, events, and resources from your Mac. </li> 
      <li>Note that&nbsp;Hype Reflect also has a console for reading&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">console.log();</code>&nbsp;events. When designing for touch devices, make sure your tappable elements are the right size for fingers. Read&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.apple.com/library/content/documentation/AppleApplications/Reference/SafariWebContent/ConfiguringWebApplications/ConfiguringWebApplications.html#//apple_ref/doc/uid/TP40002051-CH3-SW3">Configuring Web Applications</a> on Apple’s support site&nbsp;for tips on designing for touch screens. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="tips">Tips</h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Exporting to different platforms and content management systems</strong>: Please see&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/exporting-to-websites-apps-content-management-systems-and-more/799">our Exporting FAQ</a>.</li> 
      <li><strong>Decrease loading times</strong>: To improve the performance of your document,&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/decreasing-load-times-and-optimizing-performance-preparing-a-large-project-in-hype/986">optimize your site by reducing preloading and by optimizing images</a>.</li> 
      <li><strong>Apple Touch Images</strong>: When a web page is added to the home screen of an iOS device, images may be used to define icons and startup images for the various device sizes. You may define images to use for iPhone and iPad users’ home screen icons and startup/loading images.&nbsp;<br> First, add your images to your resource library, and reference them using the <code class="prettyprint">${resourcesFolderName}</code>&nbsp;variable. Use the code snippet below in the&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;…&lt;head&gt;</code>&nbsp;area to load these images. Edit the contents of the&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;…&lt;head&gt;</code>&nbsp;of your exported .html file by selecting Edit HTML Head in the Document Inspector.</li> 
     </ul>

     <h1 id="preview-amp-export">Preview &amp; Export</h1> 
     <p>This chapter covers previewing your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document on local browsers and and exporting your document to the web.</p> 
     <h2 id="preview-in-a-browser">Preview in a Browser</h2> 
     <p>By default, your system’s default browser is presented as the icon for the Preview toolbar button, and clicking the button opens your current document in the default browser. Clicking the dropdown menu next to the Preview button displays a list of all common installed browsers, and choosing from any of those browsers will both preview your document in that browser and make that browser the new default for the Preview toolbar button. To preview just the current scene being edited, choose File &gt; Preview in Browser &gt; Preview Current Scene in Browser, or Option-click the Preview toolbar button.</p> 
     <p>To preview directly on an iOS device, please see the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/reflect/">Hype Reflect</a>&nbsp;chapter.</p> 
     <p>By default, only common browsers will be shown in the Preview menus. You prevent this filtering by disabling the “Only show recommended browsers in preview menu” option in Hype’s preferences.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/HypeReflectPreviewDisclosure.png" data-src-retina="images/HypeReflectPreviewDisclosure@2x.png" width="378" height="254" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="available-preview-options">Available Preview Options</h5>
     <h2 id="exporting">Exporting</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;exports documents to HTML5. Exporting is a one-way process;&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will not read back any modifications made to the exported code. However, if you need to recreate a .hype document from an export, jump to the <a href="#document-recovery">document recovery section</a>. </p> 
     <h3 id="generated-html">Generated HTML</h3> 
     <p>To generate HTML, choose File &gt; Export as HTML5 &gt; Folder. By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will create a folder containing two items:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportingHTMLDoc.png" data-src-retina="images/ExportingHTMLDoc@2x.png" width="393" height="237" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="an--html-document">An .html document</h5> 
     <p>Open this HTML document in your browser to see your document in action. If you need to put your content into a different document, see <a href="#embedding-in-other-html-documents">Embedding in Other HTML Documents</a>. </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportingResourcesContents.png" data-src-retina="images/ExportingResourcesContents@2x.png" width="414" height="165" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="a-resources-folder">A resources folder</h5> 
     <p>This folder contains all image, video, and file resources stored in the document, along with these files:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>HYPE-###.full.min.js</strong>&nbsp;— The main runtime for Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents. Contains entire runtime including JavaScript required by IE6–8 for compatibility. </li> 
      <li><strong>HYPE-###.thin.min.js</strong>&nbsp;— The main runtime for Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents used by modern browsers. </li> 
      <li>HYPE-###.waypoints.min.js - Included when using Viewport actions.</li> 
      <li><strong>documentName_hype_generated_script.js</strong>&nbsp;— The document-specific data which defines all scenes, timelines, elements, and animations for the document.</li> 
      <li><strong>PIE.htc</strong>&nbsp;— An HTML component for Internet Explorer, used in Internet Explorer 6 through 8 to improve browser compatibility. See <a href="http://css3pie.com/">css3pie.com</a>&nbsp;for more info.</li> 
      <li><strong>blank.gif</strong>&nbsp;— A special image which improves transparent GIF rendering in Internet Explorer 6 through 8.</li> 
      <li><strong>cache.manifest</strong>&nbsp;— Enumerates the document’s resources for offline caching. Only present if the Create Offline Application Cache option is enabled in the Document inspector.</li> 
      <li><strong>####-restorable.plist</strong>&nbsp;— Document restoration file which can be used to recover the original Hype document from the exported content. Learn more about recovery in the Document Recovery section later in this chapter.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="export-options">Export Options</h3> 
     <p>At export time, there are several different options you can toggle:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/exportOptions.jpg" data-src-retina="images/exportOptions@2x.jpg" width="502" height="299"></p> 
     <h5 id="export-options">Export Options</h5> 
     <p><strong>Also save .html file</strong></p> 
     <p>If this is enabled, it will output the HTML file mentioned above. Disabling this option is useful if you’ve made modifications to the HTML file and do not want it to be overwritten, or if you have a different HTML file you are using instead.</p> 
     <p><strong>Include text contents for search engines</strong></p> 
     <p>When enabled, Hype will include all of the text found in your document’s elements in special hidden text elements appended to the HTML file. Those text elements help your document be indexed by Google and other search engines.</p> 
     <p><strong>Create enclosing folder</strong></p> 
     <p>When this is enabled,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will create a top-level folder containing the .html file and the *.hyperesources folder. Disable this option if you want&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;to only write these in the specified folder.</p> 
     <h3 id="image-optimization">Image Optimization</h3> 
     <p>To help minimize document size, improve compatibility with all browsers, and improve rendering on high resolution “retina” displays,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will by default:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Convert non-web safe images —&nbsp;any image that is not a PNG, JPEG, GIF, or SVG —&nbsp;to a PNG or JPEG. If the source image has any transparency,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will convert it to a PNG to preserve that transparency. Otherwise the non-web safe image is converted to a JPEG to minimize size.</li> 
      <li>Resize images so they’re only as large as is needed for the document. For example, if you use an 18 megapixel 5184px × 3456px image as the background for a 600px × 400px scene,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will resize the image on export and reduce the final download size by several megabytes.</li> 
      <li>Create high resolution <code class="prettyprint">_2x</code> images that will be downloaded by devices with “retina” displays, if the source image is large enough. Automatically generated high resolution images are only downloaded by devices with retina displays, so they don’t affect download times for anyone else.</li> 
      <li>Convert PNGs without transparency to JPGs if doing so reduces the file size. </li> 
      <li>Not convert animated GIFs or animated PNGs. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The following three scenarios illustrate&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s default image export behavior:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Given a 200px × 200px JPEG displayed as a 50px × 50px image,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;generates a 50px × 50px image during export that is downloaded and displayed to most users. A high resolution 100px × 100px image is also generated, and is provided to users with “retina” displays.</li> 
      <li>Given a PDF displayed as a 100px × 100px image,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will convert the first page to a 100px × 100px PNG for standard displays as well as a 200px × 200px PNG for high resolution displays.</li> 
      <li>Given a 100px × 100px image JPG named&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">file@2x.jpg</code>&nbsp;and a 50px × 50px image named <code class="prettyprint">file.jpg</code>, Tumult Hype will group the two images. The @2x image will be loaded on ‘retina’ screens, and the non-retina image will be loaded on non-retina screens.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Tumult Hype’s automatic image optimization can be disabled by choosing an image in the Resource Library and deselecting the “Automatically optimize when exporting” option. This option should be disabled if you need to <a href="referencing-resources-in-code">access the resource</a> using the <code class="prettyprint">${resourcesFolderName}</code> variable. You may select multiple images in the resource library by clicking the first element in a series, holding shift, and then selecting the last element in the series. </p> 
     <h2 id="hosting-your-document-on-the-web">Hosting Your Document on the Web</h2> 
     <p>The quickest way to host your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document on the web is to upload your exported .html file and the .hyperesources folder to your hosting provider. You can then visit the URL of your .html file to load your document.</p> 
     <p>For a video walkthrough on getting your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document on the web, please see&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/howto-uploading-your-tumult-hype-document-to-a-web-server/2125">this article</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="embedding-in-other-html-documents">Embedding in Other HTML Documents</h2> 
     <div class="js-lazyYT" data-youtube-id="-AXLJpGTGYM" data-parameters="rel=0&amp;showinfo=0&amp;color=white&amp;theme=light" data-ratio="16:9">
      Loading…
     </div> 
     <p>A good starting point for embedding is to set the export option to save the HTML file. The file is relatively bare-bones and contains three critical lines which will actually kick off the document:</p> 
     <pre class="highlight html"><code><span class="c">&lt;!-- copy these lines to your document: --&gt;</span>

<span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">id=</span><span class="s">"documentName_hype_container"</span> <span class="na">style=</span><span class="s">"position:relative;overflow:hidden;width:600px;height:400px;"</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>
    <span class="nt">&lt;script </span><span class="na">type=</span><span class="s">"text/javascript"</span> <span class="na">src=</span><span class="s">"documentName.hyperesources/documentName_hype_generated_script.js?56206"</span><span class="nt">&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</span>
<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span>

<span class="c">&lt;!-- end copy --&gt;</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p>These lines can be copied and pasted into other documents; the open/close&nbsp;div&nbsp;tags and one&nbsp;script&nbsp;tag are all you need. They reference the .hyperesources folder, which also needs to be placed at the same level as the HTML file. To open HTML files, you’ll need a HTML editor. Here are a&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/recommended-html-editors/1384">few we recommend.</a>&nbsp;Note: this example uses “documentName” as the exported document’s name, so the lines in other exported documents will be different. Please be certain to replace any instances of “documentName” with the proper document name if you’re copying directly from this example.</p> 
     <h2 id="editing-head-html">Editing Head HTML</h2> 
     <p>To edit the <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;...&lt;/head&gt;</code> of your document prior to export, click on ‘Edit HTML Head’ in the Document Inspector. Insert your CSS styles, external JavaScript references or anything else that you might need in the <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code> of an HTML document. To modify the font size of this area select Hype &gt; Preferences. For further control over exported HTML, please see Hype Export Scripts todo tk. </p> 
     <p>You may adjust the typography of the head HTML area by selecting Hype &gt; Preferences. </p> 
     <h2 id="ibooks">iBooks</h2> 
     <p>To export your&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;animation as an iBooks and Dashboard-compatible widget file, choose File &gt; Export &gt; Dashboard/iBooks Author Widget.&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers four pre-defined iBooks document sizes to choose from in the&nbsp;<a href="https://tumult.com/hype/documentation/inspectors/#document">Document inspector</a>, which are useful for creating animations specifically tailored to iBooks.</p> 
     <p>Insert Dashboard/iBooks Author Widgets into iBooks Author documents by choosing Insert &gt; Widget &gt; HTML from within iBooks Author, or dragging and dropping the exported widget into an open iBooks Author document.</p> 
     <p>If you have any additional questions not covered here, please visit the&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/c/exporting-previewing/ibooks-widget">iBooks Author HTML widget support forum</a>. If you’re interested in how a iBooks widget is built, please see our&nbsp;<a href="http://blog.tumult.com/2012/01/20/easy-html5-animations-in-ibooks-using-tumult-hype-and-ibooks-author/">blog post</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="oam-widget">OAM Widget</h2> 
     <p>To export your animation as an OAM widget, select this option. This format creates a package you can import to InDesign with DPS, Adobe Muse, or Dreamweaver. <strong>To avoid issues, do not use foreign characters or spaces in your document name during export</strong>. </p> 
     <h2 id="dropbox">Dropbox</h2> 
     <p><em>Unfortunately Dropbox <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/en/help/16">is disabling this service</a> so we have removed this feature from Tumult Hype.</em> For alternatives, please visit <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/dropbox-discontinuing-html-rendering-public-folder/7752">this forum thread</a>. </p> 
     <h2 id="accessibility-features">Accessibility Features</h2> 
     <p>Please view the <a href="#accessibility">Accessibility chapter</a> for information about building content to support screen readers and assistive devices.</p> 
     <h2 id="export-as-movie">Export as Movie</h2> 
     <p>Tumult Hype supports exporting to Video, Animated GIF, and PNG sequence. Tumult Hype Professional supports exporting to APNG and to a higher resolution video format. Choose File &gt; Export as Movie and choose your preferred format. The export dialog which appears allows you to change the duration, frame rate, and dimensions of the video, GIF, PNG sequence or APNG. Clicking Save creates the appropriate files in the location you choose.</p> 
     <p>When exporting to these formats, the duration defaults to the time it will take for all animations to finish when previewed. If a loop is detected, the duration will be set to 30 seconds. Physics-based animations do not count in the duration, so manual adjustments may be required to capture all physics simulations. Use timeline and scene actions to extend the recordable portion of your document. For example, create a Timeline Action at the end of the Main Timeline to transition to the next scene. If the animation on your first scene was 5 seconds, and the animation on your second scene was 10 seconds, the default video duration will be 15 seconds.</p> 
     <h3 id="export-as-video">Export as Video</h3> 
     <p>Note that any audio embedded in your document is not included in your export. Also note that video exporting is only supported on OS X 10.7 “Lion” and later. For information on capturing audio please <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/exporting-video-with-sound-creating-a-screencast/1131">view this forum post</a>.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/exportasMovie@2x.png" data-src-retina="images/exportasMovie@2x.png" width="753" height="626"></p> 
     <h5 id="export-as-movie-dialog">Export as Movie Dialog</h5> 
     <p>In Tumult Hype Professional, you may choose the export bitrate &amp; optionally export in the Apple ProRes 422 video format for higher resolution video. <a target="_blank" href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro/" class="profeatureinline">HYPE PRO ONLY</a></p> 
     <h3 id="export-as-animated-gif">Export as Animated GIF</h3> 
     <p>When exporting as animated GIF, please keep in mind that the format only supports 256 colors. GIF file sizes increases as you have more colors, a higher framerate, and long animations.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/exportasGIF.png" data-src-retina="images/exportasGIF@2x.png" width="571" height="293"></p> 
     <h5 id="export-as-animated-gif-dialog">Export as Animated GIF Dialog</h5>
     <h2 id="exporting-to-other-cmss-and-platforms">Exporting to Other CMSs and Platforms</h2> 
     <p>Since&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents are built in HTML, Javascript, and CSS, they can be run displayed on a large number of devices. We have covered step-by-step instructions for many platforms in this&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/exporting-to-websites-apps-content-management-systems-and-more/799">Exporting FAQ</a>.</p> 
     <h2 id="advanced-export">Advanced Export</h2> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>A typical Hype export includes all scenes, layouts, and resources. Advanced Export gives you full control over what Scenes, Layouts, and Resources are included in your export, and provides advanced control for situations where you require small download sizes. Let’s say you’re working on a series of three advertisements: </p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AdvancedExportLayouts.png" data-src-retina="images/AdvancedExportLayouts@2x.png" width="286" height="351" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="an-example-document-containing-three-separate-layouts">An example document containing three separate layouts</h5> 
     <p>When you open the Advanced Export window (File &gt; Advanced Export…) you are presented with a list of export slices representing all scenes and layouts in your document. Each slice represents a separate Hype Export complete with its own html file, resources, and Hype javascript runtime. For our advertisement example, we can quickly create three separate HTML files from a single HTML document by exporting individual layouts: </p> 
     <p><a href="images/AdvancedExportPanel@2x.png" target="_blank"><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/AdvancedExportPanel.png" data-src-retina="images/AdvancedExportPanel@2x.png" width="894" height="685" alt=""></a></p> 
     <h5 id="the-advanced-export-panel">The Advanced Export Panel</h5> 
     <p>The options above will create three separate folders, each containing separate HTML documents. </p> 
     <h3 id="slice-export-options">Slice Export Options</h3> 
     <p>Each slice represents a separate exported document. To modify the options for a slice, select it from the slice list on the left hand side and modify the slice options in the box on the right. On the right side, you can select which scenes resources to include. If a resource checkbox is disabled that means it is referenced by an element or animation in one of the selected scenes. </p> 
     <p>You can add, remove, and duplicate slices by selecting a slice and selecting an option at bottom of the Advanced Export window. Rename slices by double-clicking on the slice name. Slice names define the folder within which document content is exported. </p> 
     <p>Once you define slice options, save the current options for any new slices by selecting the ‘Default Options’ dropdown at the bottom of the panel. </p> 
     <p>The following options can be set on a per-slice basis: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Export Script</strong> - Select from the dropdown to use an <a href="#export-scripts">Export script</a>.</li> 
      <li><strong>Create Enclosing Folder</strong> – Exports your document into a folder under the document name set during export.</li> 
      <li><strong>Also save .html file</strong> – Generates an HTML file for your document. 
       <ul> 
        <li><strong>Include text contents for search engines</strong> – Includes the full text of your document within the page for search engines. </li> 
        <li><strong>Name as “index.html” (requires enclosing folder)</strong> – Creates an index.html file for each slice. </li> 
        <li><strong>Inline data file+loader</strong> – Instead of generating a JavaScript file with your document, a script will be included directly on the page. The HYPE.js file will be loaded from a regular JS file. </li> 
       </ul></li> 
      <li><strong>Support Internet Explorer 6-9</strong> – The Hype javascript runtime contains extra code to support as many features as possible on IE 6-9. If you don’t need to support IE 6-9 you can uncheck this option to reduce the export size.</li> 
      <li><strong>Use External runtime URL</strong>: Setting a runtime URL will load runtime files from an external server. <a href="#external-runtime-hosting">Learn more here</a>. </li> 
      <li><strong>Create restorable document file</strong>: For more information, view <a href="#document-recovery">Document Recovery</a>. Does not affect final download size.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="managing-custom-slice-configurations">Managing Custom Slice Configurations</h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>Creating a configuration</strong>: To create a new advanced export configuration, or <em>slice</em>, click the + button at the bottom left-hand corner of the panel. </li> 
      <li><strong>Deleting</strong>: To remove a slice configuration, select the - button while a slice is selected. </li> 
      <li><strong>Default Slices</strong>: To save a slice as the default configuration, select your slice, and select the Default Options dropdown. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="exporting-scenes-or-layouts-individually">Exporting Scenes or Layouts Individually</h3> 
     <p>Hype will automatically generate slices for exporting each layout and scene individually. You cannot modify which scenes or layouts are included in these slices, but you can change the other export and resource options. Keep in mind you can always duplicate a slice if you want to modify it.</p> 
     <p>You can export multiple slices at the same time. Simply check the box next to any slices you wish to export and click “Export Slices”.</p> 
     <h3 id="slice-file-size">Slice File Size</h3> 
     <p>At the bottom of the slice options you can view the estimated export size of the individual slice:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><strong>All Files</strong> – The on disk size of all files exported by the slice</li> 
      <li><strong>@1x Download</strong> – The estimated download size on a modern web browser running on a non-retina display</li> 
      <li><strong>@2x Download</strong> – The estimated download size on a modern web browser running on a retina display</li> 
      <li><strong>IE Download</strong> – The download size required for compatibility with Internet Explorer 6-9</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      Actual download sizes will be smaller for the majority of servers due to gzip compression. See below.
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h3 id="reducing-initial-download">Reducing Initial Download</h3> 
     <p>Advanced Export is built for bandwidth-sensitive applications such as advertising network deployments, or deployments for mobile device interfaces. Some deployments limit you based on the size of a zip file uploaded to their network, while others measure the amount of content downloaded by the end user. If you are having issues with deployment to an ad network, please visit the <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/c/advertising">Advertising category</a> in our forums. Below are a few guidelines to export with the lowest possible file size: </p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>If you don’t require IE 6-9 support, you can save several bytes by unchecking that option during export. </li> 
      <li>Tumult Hype will automatically optimize your images to ensure a retina version will be served to retina-enabled devices. If you would prefer to bypass that optimization, uncheck ‘Automatically optimize while exporting’ while selecting that image, or multiple images, in your Resource Library. </li> 
      <li>Prior to deploying your exported document to a server, drag and drop your resource folder into <a href="https://imageoptim.com/">Imageoptim</a>. This will squeeze additional bytes out of your images. </li> 
      <li>Use SVG images whenever possible. </li> 
      <li>If you control your server, <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/t/turning-on-compression-enabling-gzip-on-your-server-to-speed-up-loading-times/4762?u=daniel">enable gzip</a> to further compress content.</li> 
      <li>Delete any unused scenes, timelines, images, or keyframes.</li> 
      <li>Custom font files will typically count against your file size limit; use external font services like Google Fonts if necessary.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3 id="external-runtime-hosting">External Runtime Hosting</h3> 
     <p>To host Tumult Hype runtime files on a CDN or server of your choosing, first export a blank document with the complete runtime. Follow these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Create a document with a single ‘<a href="#viewport-actions">viewport</a>’ action. This ensures that the ‘waypoints’ JavaScript is included in your document export.</li> 
      <li>Select File &gt; Export as HTML5 &gt; Folder</li> 
      <li>Delete the <code class="prettyprint">#####-restorable.plist</code> and <code class="prettyprint">documentname_hype_generated_script.js</code> files from the exported folder.</li> 
      <li>Upload the entirety of the folder to your server. Your server should now contain: </li> 
     </ol> 
     <pre class="highlight plaintext"><code>blank.gif
HYPE-574.full.min.js
HYPE-574.thin.min.js
HYPE-574.waypoints.min.js
PIE.htc
</code></pre> 
     <p>Please note that after every Tumult Hype upgrade, you’ll need to re-export the <code class="prettyprint">HYPE-###.full.min.js</code>, <code class="prettyprint">HYPE-###.thin.min.js</code>, and HYPE-###.waypoints.min.js files. These are newly-generated for each version. The files blank.gif and PIE.htc will not change. There are no issues hosting multiple runtime versions in a single folder.</p> 
     <h2 id="document-recovery">Document Recovery</h2> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;exports a recovery file from which the original Hype document can be recreated. This file is never downloaded by users viewing your document online, so it does not impact download times. Also, the file name is randomized per-document, so that it’s not easy for someone else to download and recreate your source Tumult Hype document.</p> 
     <p>If you have lost your source Hype document, you can recover it by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Download the exported <code class="prettyprint">documentname.hyperesources</code> folder.</li> 
      <li>Choose Help &gt; Restore Document from Export and select the <code class="prettyprint">documentname.hyperesources</code> folder.</li> 
      <li>Choose where to save your recovered document.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>The recovery process re-creates your source Hype document based on what was exported. If “Automatically optimize when exporting” is checked for images, the scaled down version will be only recoverable image available. The recovery process is no replacement for a true back up system; please use a back up system like Time Machine to protect your valuable data.</p> 
     <p>If for some reason you don’t want restorable document data included in your exports, disable this behavior by deselecting the “Create restorable document file when exporting” option in Hype’s General preferences or in the Advanced Export pane. </p> 
     <h3 id="additional-questions">Additional questions?</h3> 
     <p>If you have any additional questions not covered here, please visit the&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.tumult.com/c/exporting-previewing">exporting support forum</a>.</p> 
     <h1 id="accessibility">Accessibility</h1> 
     <p>In contrast to HTML pages built with static HTML, elements are inserted into the Tumult Hype div based on the current scene, timelines playing, and layouts. Tumult Hype has a few built in features to help your visitors read and interact with your document with the help of screen readers. </p> 
     <p>This chapter goes point-by-point through the <a href="http://webaim.org/standards/508/checklist">508 Accessibility checklist</a> on Webaim.org. Additional checklists for web accessibility can be found at <a href="https://www.wuhcag.com/wcag-checklist/">wuhcag.com</a>. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>(a) A text equivalent for every non-text element shall be provided (e.g., via “alt”, “longdesc”, or in element content).</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>For image-based content, make sure you add a description in the ‘Alternate Text’ field for that element in the Identity Inspector. </p> 
     <p>To ensure users making use of screen readers can ‘tab’ to your elements, use the Tab Index value in the identity inspector. </p> 
     <p><img class="inspector" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/Inspector36Identity.png" data-src-retina="images/Inspector36Identity@2x.png" width="277" height="420" alt="Identity Inspector"></p> 
     <p><strong>Example</strong>: A button with the ‘Alternate Text’ set to ‘Submit Button’, a ‘Tab Index’ value of 6, a Unique element id set to <code class="prettyprint">nextscene-button</code>, and a class name of <code class="prettyprint">button-lrg</code> will output the following HTML during export:</p> 
     <p><code class="prettyprint">&lt;div class="HYPE_element button-lrg" id="nextscene-button" title="Next Scene" alt="Submit Button " tabindex="6" role="button" style="..."&gt;Next Scene&lt;/div&gt;</code></p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(b)</em> Equivalent alternatives for any multimedia presentation shall be synchronized with the presentation.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Video hosts like Youtube support Captions, and you can easily use external JavaScript libraries that handle subtitles. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em><code class="prettyprint">(c)</code></em> Web pages shall be designed so that all information conveyed with color is also available without color, for example from context or markup. </p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>This is more of a design guideline. Make sure that your text color and element contrast is easy to navigate and read, and consistently guides your visitors to navigate the site. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(d)</em> Documents shall be organized so they are readable without requiring an associated style sheet.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Because Hype documents are dynamic JavaScript, generated as needed based on the scene or timeline, there are not ‘stylesheets’ that we depend on. When exporting a document, Hype optionally exports content suitable for SEO. This content could also be used as the ‘noscript’ text displayed in older screen readers that do not support JavaScript. More info on <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Element/noscript">that technique</a>. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(e)</em> Redundant text links shall be provided for each active region of a server-side image map &amp; (f) Client-side image maps shall be provided instead of server-side image maps except where the regions cannot be defined with an available geometric shape.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Not applicable – Tumult Hype does not use Image Maps. </p> 
     <p>G &amp; H pertain to HTML tables, which are not a feature in Hype, but you can embed them using the inner HTML of an element. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(i)</em> Frames shall be titled with text that facilitates frame identification and navigation. </p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>To set the Title of your page, edit the field in the <a href="#inspectors">Document Inspector</a>. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(j)</em> Pages shall be designed to avoid causing the screen to flicker with a frequency greater than 2 Hz and lower than 55 Hz.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>This could happen if your animations show different colors in rapid succession – avoiding this is pretty easy. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(k)</em> A text-only page, with equivalent information or functionality, shall be provided to make a web site comply with the provisions of this part, when compliance cannot be accomplished in any other way. The content of the text-only page shall be updated whenever the primary page changes.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>To create a version that is text only, you can make use of the text-based content that Hype outputs. For example, if your scene had a header and small snippet of text Hype would output the following if you have: “Include Text Contents for Search Engines” </p> 
     <pre class="highlight html"><code><span class="c">&lt;!-- text content for search engines: --&gt;</span>

<span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">style=</span><span class="s">"display:none"</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>
    <span class="nt">&lt;div&gt;</span>My Header Text <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span>
    <span class="nt">&lt;div&gt;</span>This is element text, for example text that would be inserted in a text box or a rectangle.<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span>
<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span>

<span class="c">&lt;!-- end text content: --&gt;</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p>If you remove the enclosing div with the <code class="prettyprint">&lt;div style="display:none"&gt;</code> div and its closing div, this would be the basis for your ‘text only’ HTML page. </p> 
     <p>Placing a ‘View Text Only Version’ link near the top of your page (and with a -1 tab index value) will ensure that your visitors accessing your site with a screen reader can quickly get to that version. (It would be linked as a regular HTML page.)</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(l)</em> When pages utilize scripting languages to display content, or to create interface elements, the information provided by the script shall be identified with functional text that can be read by assistive technology. </p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>The functional text you set on your elements or buttons should have descriptive text in the ‘Alt’ field (Located in the Identity Inspector). </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(m)</em> When a web page requires that an applet, plug-in or other application be present on the client system to interpret page content, the page must provide a link to a plug-in or applet that complies with §1194.21(a) </p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>As long as you use audio or video formats recommended in our <a href="#audio-amp-video">documentation</a>, media should work without any additional applets or plugins. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(n)</em> When electronic forms are designed to be completed on-line, the form shall allow people using assistive technology to access the information, field elements, and functionality required for completion and submission of the form, including all directions and cues.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Instead of reinventing the wheel and building forms yourself with HTML / CSS and a server-side language, use a form system like <a href="https://www.surveylegend.com">Survey Legend</a> and Google Forms. <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/search?q=forms">Here’s information</a> on building input forms in Hype. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(o)</em> A method shall be provided that permits users to skip repetitive navigation links.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>This is a design recommendation: let your users get to the meat of the content quickly. <a href="http://webaim.org/techniques/skipnav/">Read this page for help</a>. </p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><em>(p)</em> When a timed response is required, the user shall be alerted and given sufficient time to indicate more time is required.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>This is a usability guideline: don’t pressure people into a countdown without a way to prolong the count. </p> 
     <h1 id="export-scripts">Export Scripts</h1> 
     <p>Export Scripts help automate workflows involving Tumult Hype’s output. A common use case is that Ad networks often need files to be zipped and in a very specific format. Once installed, Export Scripts add an item in the File &gt; Export as HTML menu and extend Tumult Hype’s UI allowing modifications to the outgoing HTML5 content. Export Scripts can be developed by anyone to augment Tumult Hype’s output. </p> 
     <p>When an export script has been installed, a new entry appears in File &gt; Export as HTML5, Advanced Export, and optionally the Preview toolbar item. Export scripts may also allow values to be input directly within the Hype interface and in the form of custom actions modified within Action panels. </p> 
     <p><strong>Sample Workflows</strong></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Produce a zip file for delivery to ad networks</li> 
      <li>Post-process images</li> 
      <li>Upload exported documents to servers via FTP, SFTP, via Amazon S3, or other services</li> 
      <li>Insert default JavaScripts into the <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code> HTML or make other HTML modifications</li> 
      <li>Define asset folder structures (use img, css, js, etc. instead of .hyperesources)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2 id="installing-export-scripts">Installing Export Scripts</h2> 
     <p>Export Scripts must have an extension recognizable as a script (.sh, .py, .rb, etc.), and must have <code class="prettyprint">hype-export</code> within their filename. For example: <code class="prettyprint">DoubleClickStudio.hype-export.py</code>. Export Scripts are installed by the user in the Application Scripts folder for Hype. This folder is dependent on how the user obtained Hype:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Tumult Store &amp; Mac App Store: <code class="prettyprint">~/Library/Application Scripts/com.tumult.Hype2/</code></li> 
      <li>Setapp: <code class="prettyprint">~/Library/Application Scripts/com.tumult.hype-setapp/</code></li> 
      <li>Beta: <code class="prettyprint">~/Library/Application Scripts/com.tumult.Beta.Hype2/</code></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Hype’s Export preference pane offers a button for the user to easily go to this folder. If the script successfully meets the above points, it will show up in the list in this pane:</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportScriptsPreferences.png" data-src-retina="images/ExportScriptsPreferences.png" width="482" height="276" alt="Hype Exports in Preferences"></p> 
     <h5 id="hype-export-scripts-in-preferences">Hype Export Scripts in Preferences</h5> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
       To transfer Scripts between users, compress it in an archive to retain permissions. Export Scripts must have permissions set as executable: chmod 755 [filename] to properly work. 
      <a href="http://www.macinstruct.com/node/415">Read more</a> about setting permissions. 
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h2 id="using-export-scripts">Using Export Scripts</h2> 
     <p>When an Export Script has been installed, you may trigger it by:</p> 
     <h3 id="selecting-it-in-the-file-gt-export-as-html5-menu">Selecting it in the File &gt; Export as HTML5 menu</h3> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportScriptsFileMenu.png" data-src-retina="images/ExportScriptsFileMenu.png" width="627" height="457" alt="Export Scripts"></p> 
     <h3 id="choosing-it-during-advanced-export">Choosing it during Advanced Export</h3> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportScriptsadvanced-export.jpg" data-src-retina="images/ExportScriptsadvanced-export.jpg" width="906" height="696" alt=""></p> 
     <h3 id="if-the-script-is-configured-to-modify-previews-you-can-find-it-in-the-preview-toolbar">If the Script is configured to modify Previews, you can find it in the Preview Toolbar:</h3> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/ExportScriptPreviewMenu.jpg" data-src-retina="images/ExportScriptPreviewMenu.jpg" width="449" height="359" alt=""></p> 
     <h2 id="developing-export-scripts">Developing Export Scripts</h2> 
     <p>For more information on building your own Export Scripts, please visit the <a href="https://github.com/tumult/hype-export-scripts">Hype Export Scripts Github Repository</a>.</p> 
     <h1 id="templates">Templates</h1> 
     <p><a href="http://tumult.com/hype/pro" alt="Learn More" title="Learn More" class="profeature">HYPE PRO ONLY<br></a></p>
     <div class="profeaturebottom"></div>
     <p></p> 
     <p>Templates are “freeze dried” Hype documents –&nbsp;opening a Hype template creates a new document based on the opened template. Any document can be saved as a template by choosing File &gt; Save Template. Once created, templates cannot be edited. Thus to change a template, you’ll want to create a new document by opening that template and then save over the old template by choosing File &gt; Save Template.</p> 
     <p>While only the Professional edition of Hype can create templates, any edition of Hype can create new documents from templates.</p> 
     <p>Visit the <a href="https://forums.tumult.com/c/template-gallery">Template Gallery</a> in the forums to check out forum member-created templates. </p> 
     <h1 id="resources">Resources</h1> 
     <p>Resources are the images, videos, JavaScript functions, and other files that have been added to a&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document. Unlike <a href="#elements">elements</a>, which are unique to each scene, resources are shared across the entire&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document. When playing back in a browser,&nbsp;only a single copy of each resource is downloaded and shared that copy across all scenes.</p> 
     <h2 id="managing-resources">Managing Resources</h2>
     <h3 id="resource-library">Resource Library</h3> 
     <p>Tumult Hype’s Resource Library offers control over a document’s resources. Open the Resource library by choosing View &gt; Resource Library or clicking the Resource toolbar button. The Resource Library offers controls for filtering and searching resources, and also provides numerous controls for managing resources.</p> 
     <h3 id="adding-resources">Adding Resources</h3> 
     <p>Clicking the Resource Library’s Plus button provides a menu from which new files can be added to or new JavaScript functions can be created in the front-most document. Any file can be added to the Resource Library and will be included in the .hyperesources folder upon export. Images and videos in the Resource Library can be added to a scene by dragging them from the Resource Library and dropping them on the scene.</p> 
     <h3 id="removing-resources">Removing Resources</h3> 
     <p>Clicking the Minus button removes any resources that aren’t actively used by elements in the document’s scenes. Any images and videos that are currently used in the document cannot be deleted until all elements using those resources have first been deleted.</p> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;automatically deletes image and video resources when all elements using those resources have themselves been deleted. To prevent this behavior so that images and videos persist in the document even after all elements using those resources have been deleted, deselect the “Remove when no longer referenced” checkbox.</p> 
     <h3 id="updating-resources">Updating Resources</h3> 
     <p>Every time a file-based resource is added to a&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;stores a copy of the file in the document and also keeps a link to the original file. Whenever the original file is modified,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;automatically prompts to see if the copy stored in the current&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document should be updated to match the original file outside of&nbsp;Tumult Hype. Clicking the Refresh button manually updates the file. Sometimes the connection between the original files and&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s copy is broken; this often happens when the&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document is moved to a different computer, or if the original source file is saved under a different name. Should this happen,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;displays a Choose dialog so you can find the original file, restore the connection, and update the current&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;document’s copy of the file.</p> 
     <h3 id="replacing-resources">Replacing Resources</h3> 
     <p>To replace any file-based resource with a different file, click the Replace button. The Choose dialog which appears lets you pick the replacement file. This is a very powerful tool for quickly replacing all copies of an image or video across all scenes in a document.</p> 
     <h3 id="resource-groups">Resource Groups</h3> 
     <p>Images, videos, and audio resources all create resource groups, where one resource references multiple files. Resource groups are used to collect different file variants which may be used by the resource in different contexts. Audio and video resource groups have place holders for the different file encodings which are required by browsers, and image resource groups offer place holders for standard resolution images and “@2x” images. It’s important to note that adding additional files to a resource group will not adversely affect the document’s download time: browsers will only ever download the single file they need from a resource group, ignoring the other files in the group.</p> 
     <p>To add additional audio or video sources to a resource group, select the grayed out source in the Resource Library, click the Add Source button, and then choose the appropriate audio, video, or image file. For example, a “video/webm” resource may be added to the Video2 resource group shown on the right. Additional sources can also be dragged onto the Resource Library, and Hype will attempt to add those resources to the correct resource group.</p> 
     <h2 id="resource-optimization">Resource Optimization</h2>
     <h3 id="controlling-preloading">Controlling Preloading</h3> 
     <p>By default,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents preload all image resources before beginning any animation. This is done to ensure viewers always see the document as it appears in&nbsp;Tumult Hype, with no missing images. This behavior can be disabled on a per-image basis by first choosing an image from the resource list and then deselecting the Preload checkbox. Videos are not preloaded so there is no control for this behavior. To turn off preloading for multiple images, select the ‘images’ filter at the top of the resources library, and select the first image, hold shift, and click the last image. You may then uncheck ‘preload’ at the bottom of the resource library. </p> 
     <h3 id="image-optimization">Image Optimization</h3> 
     <p>To help minimize document size, improve compatibility with all browsers, and improve rendering on high resolution “retina” displays,&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;will optimize images. Please see <a href="#image-optimization">Image Optimization</a> for more information. </p> 
     <h2 id="advanced-resources">Advanced Resources</h2>
     <h3 id="including-css-and-javascript-in-document-code-classprettyprintltheadgtcode">Including CSS and JavaScript in Document <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code></h3> 
     <p>When CSS or JavaScript files are tracked by a document’s Resource Library, Tumult Hype&nbsp;can automatically include references to those files in the document’s header when exporting. This behavior is the default; to disable, choose the CSS or JavaScript file which should not be included in the document’s header and deselect the “Include in document &lt;head&gt;” checkbox.</p> 
     <h3 id="referencing-resources-in-code">Referencing Resources in Code</h3> 
     <p>Because resources stored in&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;documents are exported into an animation’s resources folder, you may reliably refer to them in the document’s <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code> or in JavaScript functions created within&nbsp;Tumult Hype using the <code class="prettyprint">${resourcesFolderName}</code> variable.</p> 
     <h3 id="in-a-documents-code-classprettyprintltheadgtcode-or-an-elements-inner-html">In a Document’s <code class="prettyprint">&lt;head&gt;</code> or an Element’s Inner HTML</h3> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;provides a special HTML variable,&nbsp;<code class="prettyprint">${resourcesFolderName}</code>, which always references the resources folder Tumult Hype&nbsp;creates when exporting and previewing a document. Use this variable anywhere a URL path is expected. For example, after adding the file jquery-1.8.2.min.js to your document using the Resource Library, reference that file in your document’s <code class="prettyprint">head</code> with:</p> 
     <pre class="highlight html"><code><span class="nt">&lt;script </span><span class="na">src=</span><span class="s">"${resourcesFolderName}/jquery-1.8.2.min.js"</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span><span class="err"> </span></code></pre> 
     <p>Similarly, after adding the image globe.png to your document, you could refer to the image in an element’s inner HTML with</p> 
     <pre class="highlight html"><code><span class="nt">&lt;img</span> <span class="na">src=</span><span class="s">"${resourcesFolderName}/globe.png"</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p>Please note that you should deselect ‘Automatically optimize when exporting’ in the resource library to access an image resource’s original file. A file may be optimized and exported under a different name based on image optimization rules.</p> 
     <h3 id="in-javascript-functions">In JavaScript Functions</h3> 
     <p>Tumult Hype&nbsp;offers a JavaScript API for returning the string value of the document’s resources folder URL: <code class="prettyprint">hypeDocument.resourcesFolderURL()</code>. Use this in any JavaScript functions to reliably access the document’s associated resources folder. For example, if the document had an image named logo.png, the image’ path could be constructed in a JavaScript function via</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="kd">var</span> <span class="nx">logoImagePath</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nx">hypeDocument</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">resourcesFolderURL</span><span class="p">()</span> <span class="o">+</span><span class="s2">"/logo.png"</span><span class="p">;</span>
</code></pre> 
     <h1 id="javascript">JavaScript</h1>
     <h2 id="using-javascript">Using JavaScript</h2>
     <h3 id="creating-a-new-javascript">Creating a new JavaScript</h3> 
     <p><img align="right" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/JavaScriptNewFunction.png" data-src-retina="images/JavaScriptNewFunction@2x.png" width="280" height="153" alt=""></p> 
     <p>JavaScript functions within&nbsp;Tumult Hype&nbsp;are generally run in response to user events. In any action panel, such as the panels found in the Mouse Actions inspector, create a JavaScript function by following these steps:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Click the Plus button in the action’s header to add a new action.</li> 
      <li>Click the Action menu and choose Run JavaScript.</li> 
      <li>Click the Function menu and choose New Function.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>This will open a new JavaScript Editor tab where custom JavaScript functions can be written. A sample JavaScript function looks like the following:</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="kd">function</span> <span class="nx">untitledFunction</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">hypeDocument</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nx">element</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nx">event</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>
  <span class="nx">alert</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'Hello World'</span><span class="p">);</span>
 <span class="p">}</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p>You can edit the name of the function by editing the “untitledFunction” portion of the code or by editing the name in the Resource Library. JavaScript function names must not start with a number. Function code can only be inserted between the curly brackets <code class="prettyprint">{...}</code>. The portion&nbsp;(hypeDocument, element, event)&nbsp;is required and therefore not editable. </p> 
     <h3 id="javascript-documentation-viewer">JavaScript Documentation Viewer</h3> 
     <p>The Documentation Viewer below the editing area can be helpful for quickly building JavaScript functions based on API functions.&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s Documentation Viewer provides in-app documentation for all of&nbsp;Tumult Hype’s JavaScript API functions, and also allows functions to be quickly inserted into the JavaScript editor. To insert any function:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li>Place the editor’s cursor where you want the function to be inserted.</li> 
      <li>Select the JavaScript function you wish to be inserted.</li> 
      <li>Click the Insert button <img src="images/javascriptInsertSnippet1-6.png" width="20"> to the right of the function name.</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Functions can also be inserted by dragging-and-dropping them from the functions listing or by double-clicking their row.</p> 
     <p><img class="center" src="images/bg.png" data-src="images/JavaScriptDocumentationViewer.png" data-src-retina="images/JavaScriptDocumentationViewer@2x.png" width="835" height="340" alt=""></p> 
     <h5 id="the-javascript-documentation-viewer">The JavaScript Documentation Viewer</h5>
     <h2 id="api-functions">API Functions</h2> 
     <p><span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span> offers many JavaScript APIs to control various aspects of a document. These APIs can be called both by JavaScript functions written within <span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span>, and by scripts external to the document.</p> 
     <h2 id="document-functions">Document Functions</h2> 
     <h4 style="display:none;" id="documentName"></h4> 
     <h4 id="code-classprettyprinthypedocument-documentnamecode"><code class="prettyprint">hypeDocument.documentName()</code></h4> 
     <p>Returns the name of the document. This value can be used in the global <span class="codesnippet">HYPE.documents[documentName]</span>.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="documentId">hypeDocument.documentId()</h4> 
     <p>Returns the id of the container div for the document. This value can be used with <span class="codesnippet">document.getElementId()</span> to retrieve the container element itself.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="resourcesFolderURL">hypeDocument.resourcesFolderURL()</h4> 
     <p>Returns the string value for the document’s resources folder URL. Use this to reference assets added via the Resource Library.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="functions">hypeDocument.functions()</h4> 
     <p>Returns an array of all user-defined JavaScript functions in the <span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span> Document.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="getElementById">hypeDocument.getElementById(id)</h4> 
     <p>Searches the current document for the specified id (entered through the Identity inspector’s “Unique Element ID”) and returns the DOM HTML Element. This is similar to the typical <span class="codesnippet">document.getElementById</span>, however the API version should be used instead as <span class="notranslate">Tumult Hype</span> may reassign ids in cases of collision.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="getElementProperty">hypeDocument.getElementProperty(element, propertyName)</h4> 
     <p>Gets a property of an element based on the Hype runtime’s knowledge. The element argument must be a DOM element, generally obtained by the <code class="prettyprint">hypeDocument.getElementById()</code> function. </p> 
     <p>Valid property names (quotes required):</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="s1">'top'</span>
<span class="s1">'left'</span>
<span class="s1">'width'</span>
<span class="s1">'height'</span>
<span class="s1">'rotateZ'</span>
<span class="s1">'scaleX'</span>
<span class="s1">'scaleY'</span>
<span class="s1">'opacity'</span>
<span class="s1">'z-index'</span>
</code></pre> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="setElementProperty">hypeDocument.setElementProperty(element, propertyName, value, optionalDuration, optionalTimingFunctionName)</h4> 
     <p>Sets a property of an element in a manner compatible with the Hype runtime. If the <code class="prettyprint">optionalDuration</code> is provided, it will perform a transition animation from the current value to the specified value over the specified number of seconds. The default value is 0.</p> 
     <p>The element argument must be a DOM element, generally obtained by the <code class="prettyprint">hypeDocument.getElementById()</code> function. </p> 
     <p>Valid property names (quotes required):</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="s1">'top'</span>
<span class="s1">'left'</span>
<span class="s1">'width'</span>
<span class="s1">'height'</span>
<span class="s1">'rotateZ'</span>
<span class="s1">'scaleX'</span>
<span class="s1">'scaleY'</span>
<span class="s1">'opacity'</span>
<span class="s1">'z-index'</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p><code class="prettyprint">optionalTimingFunction</code> will default to ‘easeinout’ if not provided. Valid timing function names include (quotes required):</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="s1">'easeinout'</span>
<span class="s1">'easein'</span>
<span class="s1">'easeout'</span>
<span class="s1">'linear'</span>
</code></pre> 
     <p>To perform an <em>instant</em> transition, the optionalDuration does not need to be set because the value default is 0. </p> 
     <p><strong>Example:</strong> Use the height of element 1 (tower) to match the height of another (tree) using an <code class="prettyprint">easeout</code> transition over 2 seconds: </p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="kd">var</span> <span class="nx">towerHeight</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nx">hypeDocument</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">getElementProperty</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">tower</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'height'</span><span class="p">);</span>
<span class="nx">hypeDocument</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">setElementProperty</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">tree</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'height'</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nx">towerHeight</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">2.0</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'easeout'</span><span class="p">)</span>
</code></pre> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="relayoutIfNecessary">hypeDocument.relayoutIfNecessary()</h4> 
     <p>Explicitly tells the document to relayout all elements and groups for the current scene when using a flexible layout. Use if you have externally changed the bounding size of the main container.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="triggerCustomBehaviorNamed">hypeDocument.triggerCustomBehaviorNamed(‘customBehaviorName’)</h4> 
     <p>Informs any elements which have a custom behavior with customBehaviorName to run its actions.</p> 
     <h2 id="scene-functions">Scene Functions</h2> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="sceneNames"></h4>
     <h4>hypeDocument.sceneNames()</h4> 
     <p>Returns a list of all scenes in the document.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="currentSceneName">hypeDocument.currentSceneName()</h4> 
     <p>Returns the string value for the currently shown scene.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="showSceneNamed">hypeDocument.showSceneNamed(sceneName, optionalTransition, optionalDuration)</h4> 
     <p>Changes to the specified scene. If the optionalTransition is not specified it will default to the instant transition. See below for a list of valid transition constants.</p> 
     <p>The optionalDuration parameter is given in seconds; the default value is 1.1.</p> 
     <p></p>
     <aside class="notice">
      <p></p> 
      <p>Scene names are user-defined and uniqueness is not enforced. If you are going to use this function, be sure that no two scenes in any document have the same name.</p> 
      <p></p>
     </aside>
     <p></p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="showNextScene">hypeDocument.showNextScene(optionalTransition, optionalDuration)</h4> 
     <p>Shows the next scene, based on the order in the scene selector interface. If the optionalTransition is not specified it will default to the instant transition. See below for a list of valid transition constants.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="showPreviousScene">hypeDocument.showPreviousScene(optionalTransition, optionalDuration)</h4> 
     <p>Shows the previous scene, based on the order in the scene selector interface. If the optionalTransition is not specified it will default to the instant transition. See below for a list of valid transition constants.</p> 
     <h2 id="layout-functions">Layout Functions</h2> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="hypeDocument.layoutsForSceneNamed">hypeDocument.layoutsForSceneNamed(sceneName)</h4> 
     <p>Returns a list of layout info for the given scene. Layout info is given as an object with the following keys:</p> 
     <pre class="highlight javascript"><code><span class="s1">'name'</span>
<span class="s1">'breakpoint'</span>
<span class="s1">'width'</span>
<span class="s1">'height'</span>
</code></pre> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="hypeDocument.currentLayoutName">hypeDocument.currentLayoutName()</h4> 
     <p>Returns the string value for the name of the currently shown layout.</p> 
     <h4 class="notranslate" id="hypeDocument.showLayoutNamed">hypeDocument.showLayoutNamed(layoutName)</h4> 
     <p>Changes instantly to the specified layout in the current scene. The layout may change back on a resize event, scene change, or <code class="prettyprint">relayoutIfNecessary()</code>` call.</p>
